                  Kyng Pryamus sone of Troye
               In louyng / how hys auentures felle
               From woo to wele / and after out of Ioye
               My purpos is / or that I parte froye
               Thesipho ne thow help me for to endyte
               These woful verses / that wepyn as I wryte
            
            
               To the clepe I goddesse of turment / 
               Thou cruel fury / sorowyng euer in payne
               Help me that am the sorowful instrument
               That help louers / as I can to playne
               For wel sitte / the sooth for to sayne
               A woful wyght / to haue a drery fere
               
                  And to a sorowful tale / a sory chere
            
            
               For I that god of louys seruauntis serue
               Ne dar not loue / for myn vnlyklynesse
               Pray for spede / al shuld I therfore sterue
               So fer am I / from hys help in derknesse
               But natheles / yif thys may do gladnesse
               To ony louer / and hys lady auayle
               Haue he the thank / and myn be the trauayle
            
            
               But ye loners that bathen in gladnesse
               Yf ony drope of pyte in yow be
               Remembre yow in passyd heuynesse
               That ye han felt / and in the aduersite
               Of other folk / and thynk how that ye
               Haue felt how loue durst yow dysplease
               Or ye haue wonne hem wyth to grete ease
            
            
               
                  And pray for hem that ben in the caas
               Of Troylus as ye may after here
               That loue hym bryng / in heuene to solace
               
                  And eke for me prayeth / to god so dere
               That I haue myght / to shewe in som̄e manere
               Such peyne & woo / as louys seruaūtis endure
               As in Troylus vnsely aduenture

                  And byddyth eke for hem that ben dyspayred
               
               In loue / that neuer wyl recouered be
               
                  And eke for theym that falsly ben apeyred
               
               Thurgh wykked tunges / be yt he or she
               Thus prayeth god / for hys benygnyte
               So graūt hym soone / out of thys world to pace
               That is dyspeyred out of louys grace
            
            
               
                  And byddyth eke for hem / that ben at ease
               That god graunt hem ay / good

                   perseueraunce
               And send hem myght / their ladyes for to please
               That is to loue by worshyp and plesaunce
               For so hope I my self best auaunce
               To pray for hem that loues seruauntis be
               
                  And wryte theyr woo / and lyue in charyte
            
            
               
                  And for to haue on theym compassioun
               As though they were theyr owne brethern dere
               Now herkenyth wyth good entencioun
               For now I wil go streyght to my matere
               Iy whyche ye may the double sorow here
               Of Troylus in louyng of Criseyde
               
                  And how she forsooke hym or he deyde

               Now fyl it soo that in the toun ther was
               
                  Dwellyng a lord of grete auctoryte
               A grete deuynour / that clepyd was Calcas
               That in science so expert was he
               Knewe wel that Troye shuld destroyed be
               By answere of hys god / that hyght thus
               Dan Phebus or Appollo Delphycus
            
            
               
               So whan calcas knewe by calculyng
               
               
                  And eke by answer of thys Apollo
               That grekis shuld suche a peple bryng

               For wele he wys

                  And to the grekis went ful pryuely
               He stale anon and they in curteys wyse
               Hym dyden both worshyp and seruyse
               In trust that he had connyng hem to rede
               In euery peryle / whyche that stood in drede
            
            
               Noyse vp roos whan it was fyrst espyed
               
               In alle the toun / and openly was spoken
               That calcas traytour fled / was and alyed
               
               To hem of grece / and cast was to be wroken
               On hym that falsely hath hys fayth so broken
               
                  And sayd he and alle hys kynne attones
               Were worthy to be brent bothe fel and bones
            
            
               Now had Calcas left in thys myschaunce
               Vnwyst of thys fals and wykked dede
               A doughter whyche that was in grete penaūce
               
                  And of her lyf she was ful sore in drede
               
                  And wyst neuer what best was to rede
               
                  And as a wydewe was she al alone

               Criseide was thys ladyes name a ryght
               As to my dome in al Troyes citee
               Most fayrest lady for passyng euery wyght
               So Aungelyk shone hyr natyf beaute
               That thyng none mortal femyd she
               
                  And ther wyth was she so perfyte a creature
               As she had be made in scornyng of nature
            
            
               
               Thys lady that alday / herd at ere
               Hyr fader shame / falshed and treason
               Ful nygh out of hyr wyt / for sorow & fere
               In wydewes habyte large of samy te broun
               Byfore Hector on knees she fyl adoun
               Hys mercy lad / hyr self excusyng
               
               Wyth pytous voys / and tenderly wepyng

               But how thys town com to distruction
               Ne fallyth not to purpos me to telle
               For it were here a long dygressioun
               Fro my matyer / and yow ful long to dewlle
               But the Troian gestis as they telle
               In Omere in Dares / or in Dyte
               Who so that can may rede hem as they wryte
            
            
               And though ye greekis theym of Troie shet
                     •
                  en
               
                  Had and theyr atre besiegyd al aboute
               Yet for alle theyr vsage wold they not letten
               To worship & honour they goddis ful deuoute
               Wyth most reuerence in honour out of doute
               They worshypped a reliquyk callid Palladion
               On whom was alle theyr trust aboue echon
            
            
               
                  And so byfel whan comen was the tyme
               Of Apryll whan clothyd is the m
                     •

               In sundry wyse shewyd as I rede
               The folke of Troye theyr obseruaunces old
               
               Palladion feste wente for to hold
               
            
            
               Vnto the temple in alther beste wyse
               Generally theyr wente many a wyght
               To berkene of Palladion seruyce
               
                  And namely many a lusty knyght
               
                  And many a lady fressh and mayden bryght
               Ful wel arayed both mest and lest
               Both for the season and the hye fest
            
            
               
                  Among thise other folk was Criseyda
               In wydewes habyte black / but natheles
               Ryght as our first lettir is now an A
               In beawte fyrst / so stode the makeles
               Her goodly lookyng / gladdyd alle the pres
               Nas neuer seen thyng to be preysed derre
               Nor vnder clowd black so bryght a sterre
            
            
               
               As was Criseyde / as folke sayd echone
               That her beheld in her black weede
               
                  And yet she stood ful lowe and styl alone
               
                  Behynd other folk in lytel brede
               
                  And nye the dore vnder shames drede
               Symple of atyre / and debonayre of chyere
               Wyth ful assuryd lookyng and manyere

                  And with y• word he wold cast vp the browe

               At whiche the god of loue gan loken rowe
               Ryght for despyte / and shoope to be wroken
               He kyd anon / hys lowe was not broken
               For sodaynly be hyt hym at the ful
               
                  And yet as prowd a pecok can he pul
            
            
               
               O blynd world / O blynd entencioun
               How oft fallyth alle theffes contrarye
               Of sur quydrye and foul presumpcioun
               For caught is prowd & caught is debonayre
               Thys Troylus is clombyn on the stayre
               
                  And lytel wenyth that he shall descenden
               But alday faylith thyng / that foolis wenden
            
            
               As prowd bayard begynnyth for to skyp
               Out of the way / so prykyth hym hys corn
               Tyl he a lassh haue of the long-whyp
               Than thynkyth he though I praunce al byforn
               Fyrst in the trays / ful fat and newe y shorn
               Yet am I but an hors / and horses lawe
               I must endure / and wyth my feeris drawe
            
            
               So fierd it by this fyers and prowd kynyght
               Though he a worthy kynge sones were
               
                  And wend nothyng had had suche myght
               Agenst hys wyl that shuld hys hert stere
               Yet wyth a looke hys hert way a fuyre
               That be that now was most in pryde aboue
               Wax sodaynly most subgect vnto loue
            
            
               For thy ensample take of thys man
               Ye wyse prowde and worthy folkes alle
               To scorne loue / whyche that so soone can
               The fredom of yowre hertis to hym thralle
               For euer it was and euer be shall
               That loue is he / that all thyng may bynde
               For noman may fordo the lawe of kynde
            
            
               That this is sooth is prouyd and doth yit
               For thys trow I ye knowen alle and som̄e
               Men reden not that folk haue gretter wyt
               Than they yt han ben most wyth loue y nome
               
                  And strengest folk be therwyth ouercome
               The worthyest and grettest of degre
               Thys was and is / and yet men shul it fee
            
            
               
               
                  And trewly it fallyth wel to be soo
               For alther wysest han therwyth ben pleasid
               
               
                  And they that han ben althermost in woo
               Wyth loue haue ben conforted most and easid
               
               
                  And oft it hath the cruel hert apeasid
               
               
                  And worthy folk made worthyer of name
               
                  And causith most to drede vyce and shame
            
            
               Now sith it may not goodely be wythstonde
               
                  And is a thyng so vertuous in kynde
               Refusith not in loue to bounde
               Sith as hym self lyst he may yow bynde
               The yerd is better that bowen wyl and wynde
               Than that that brestith / and therfor I yow rede
               To folowe loue / that yow so wel can lede
            
            
               But forth to telle / in especyal
               As of this kynge sone of whyche I told
               
               And lete other thynges collateral
               Of hym thynk I my tale forth to hold
               
               Both of hys Ioye and of hys cares cold
               
               
                  And all hys werkis towchnyg thys matere
               For ther as I gan I wyl therto refere
            
            
               Within the temple he wēte hym forth pleyeng
               
               Thys Troilus of euery wight aboute
               On thys lady and now on that lokyng
               
               Whether so she were of towne or of wythoute
               
                  And vpon caas byfel that thurgh a Yowte
               Hys eye perad and so depe it went
               Al on Criseide it smet and there it stent
            
            
               
                  And sodaynly he wax therwyth astonyed
               
               
                  And gan hyr bet behold in thryfty wyse
               O mercy god thought he / wher hast yu 
                  woned
               
               That art so fayre and goodly to deuyse
               Therwyth hys herte began to sprede and ryse
               
                  And soft sighed / lest men myght hym here
               
                  And caught agayn hys fyrst pleyeng chere
            
            
               
               She was nat wyth the leste / of hyr stature
               But alle her lymmes / so wel answeryng
               
               Weren to wommanhode / that creature
               Nas neuer lasse mannyssh in semyng
               
               
                  And eke the pure wyse of her meuyng
               
               
                  Shewyd wele that men myght in her gesse
               Honour estate / and wommanly noblesse
            
            
               Tho Troilns ryght wonderly wel withal
               Gan for to lyke her meuyng and hyr chyere
               Whyche sumdel deynous was for she leete fal
               Hyr looke a lyte asyde in suche manece
               Askaunce what may I nat stond here
               
                  And after that her lookyng gan she lyght
               Hym neuer thought haue seen so good a sight
            
            
               
                  And of hyr looke in hym ther gan quyken
               So grete desire / and suche affectioun
               That hys hert bottum it gan styken
               Of hyr fygure wyth deepe oppressioun
               
                  And though he eerst had powred vp & doun
               He was tho glad / hys hornes in to shrynke
               Vnneth wist he how to looke or wynke
            
            
               Lo he that leete hym self so connyng
               
               
                  And scorned theym that louys peynes dryen
               Was ful vnware / that loue hath his dwellyng
               
               Within the subtyl streames / of hyr eyen
               That sodaynly hym thought he shuld dyen
               Ryght wyth hyr looke the spyrit in hys hert
               
                  Blissed he loue / that can thus folk conuert
            
            
               She thus in black / lykyng to Troylus
               Ouer al thyng / he stode to beholde
               Ne hys desyre / ne wherfor he stode thus
               He neuer chyere made / ne word told
               
               But from after / hys maner to behold
               
               On other thyng somtyme hys looke he caste
               
                  And eft on hyr whyle the seruyse laste
            
            
               
               
                  And after thys not fully al awapyd
               
               Out of the temple / al easily be went
               
                  Repentyng hym that he had euer Iapyd
               
               Of louie folk / lest fully the descent
               Of scorn fyl on hym self / but what he ment
               Lest it were wyst in ony maner syde
               Hys woo he gan dyssimulen / and to hyde
            
            
               Whan he was fro the temple thus departed
               
               He streyght anon / vnto hys palays turnyth
               Right with hir look thurh shot & thurh dar tid
               So feyneth he in lust / ther he soiournyth
               
                  And al his chere & speche / also he bournyth
               
                  And ay of louys seruauntis / euery whyle
               Hym self to wicke at hem he gan to smple

               Ye louers for the connyngest of yow

               But for al thys / whan that he sawe hys tyme
               He held his peas noke other boote hym gayned
               For loue bygan hys fethyrs for to lyme
               That wel vnneth vnto hys folk he feyned
               
               That other besy nedis / hym dystrayned
               
               For wo was hym that what to do he nyst
               But bad hys folk go wher that hem lyst
            
            
               
                  And whan that he in chambre was alone
               He doun vpon hys beddis feete hym sette
               
                  And fyrst he gan do sigh / and eft to grone
               
                  And thought ay so on hyr / wythouten lette
               That as he sat and woke / hys spirit mette
               That he her sawe temple and alle the guyse
               Ryght of her looke / and gan it newe aduyse
            
            
               Thus gan he make a myrrour of hys mynde
               In whyche he sawe al hool hyr fygure
               
                  And that he wel coude / in hys hert fynde
               It was to hym a ryght good auenture
               To loue suche one / and yf he dyd hys cure
               To seruen hyr yit myght he fal in grace
               Or ellis for one of hyr seruauntis pace
            
            
               
                  Imagynyng that trauayle ne grame
               Ne myght not for so goodely one be lorn
               As she ne hym for no desyre ne shame
               Al wers it wyst / but in pryce vp born
               Of al louers wel more than byforn
               Thus argued he in hys begynnyng
               
               Ful vnauysed of hys woo comyng
               
            
            
               Thus toke he purpos / louys craft to syewe
               
                  And thought he wold werke pryuely
               Fyrst to hyde hys desire in mewe
               From euery wyght y born vttirly
               But he myght ought recouered be therby
               
                  Remembryng hym that loue to wyde y blowe
               Yeldith vetter fruyt though swete seede be sowe
            
            
               
               
                  And ouer al thys moche more he thought
               What for to speke / and what to hold ynne
               
                  And to art her to loue he fought
               
                  And a song / anon ryght to begynne
               
                  And gan lowd on hys sorow for to wynne
               For wyth good hope / he gan fully assent
               Cryseyde for to loue / and not to repente

               Al styerles / wythin a bote am I
               Amydde the see betwyn wyndes two
               That in contrary stondyn euermo
               Alas what is thys wondyr maladye
               For hete of cold / for cold of hete I dye
            
            
               
               
                  And to the god of loue thus sayd he
               Wyth pytous voys / O lord now yowre is
               My spirit whyche that ought yowris be
               Yow thank I lord / yt haue me brought to this
               But whether goddesse or womman ywis
               She be I note whyche that ye do me serue
               But as hyr man I wyl ay lyue and sterue
            
            
               Ye stonden in her eyen / myghtyly
               As in a place / vnto your vertu dygne
               Therfor lord yf my seruyce or I
               May lyke yow / so be to me benygne
               For myn estate Royal / I here resigne
               In to her hande / and wyth ful humble chere
               Bycome hyr man as to my lady dere
            
            
               In hym ne deyned to spare blood Royal
               The fyre of loue wherfrom god me blesse
               Ne hym forbare in no degre for al
               hys excellent or vertuous prowesse
               But held hym as hys thral / in loue dystresse
               
                  And brent hym so in sondry wyse al newe
               That sixty tyme a day / he lost hys hewe
            
            
               So moche day from day / hys owne thought
               For lust to hyr / gan quyken and encreace
               That euery other charge he sette at nought
               For thy sul oft / hys hote fyre to ceace
               To see her goodly chere he gan to preace
               For therby to be eased wel he wend
               
               
                  And ay the nere he was / the more he brend
               
            
            
               But whan he had a space / from hys care
               Thus to hym self / ful oft he gan to pleyne
               He sayd a foole / now art thou in the snare
               That whylom Iapydest / at loues peyne
               Now art yu bent / now gnaw thyn owne cheyne
               Thou were ay wont / eche louer to reprehende
               Of thynge the which thou canst the not defende
            
            
               
               What wyl now euery louer / say of the
               If thys be wyst / but euer in thyn absence
               Laugh in scorn / and sey lo wher goth he
               That is the man / of so grete sapyence
               That held vs louers / lest in reuerence
               Now thanked be god / he may go in the daūce

                  And of my speede / be thyn alle the swetnesse
            
            
               
               Tho Troilus gan doun / on hys knees fall
               
                  And Pandare in hys armes / hent fast
               
                  And sayd now fy on the grekis all
               Yit parde god shal help vs at the laste
               
                  And dredeles yf that my lyf may laste
               
                  And god to forn / yit som̄e of hem shal smert
               
                  And yit me athynketh thys auaunt me astert
            
            
               Now pandarus / I can no more seye
               But thou wise / yu wost / thou mayst / thou art al
               My lyf my deth / hool in thyn hand I leye
               Help now quod he / yis by my trowth I shal
               
                  God yeld the frend / and thys in special
               
                  Quod Troylus / that thou me recomanude
               To her that may me / to deth comaunde
            
            
               Thys Pandarus / tho desirous to serue
               Hys ful frend / tho sayd in thys manere
               Farwel and thynk I wyl / thy thank deserue
               Haue here my trowth / & that thou shalt wel here
               
                  And went hys wey / thynkyng on thys matere
               
                  And how he myght best / byseche her of grace
               
                  And fynd a tyme herto / and a place
            
            
               For euery wyght / that hath an hous to found
               
               Ne rennyth not / the werke for to begynne
               With rakil hand / but he wyl byde a stound
               
               
                  And send hys hertis lyne / out from wythynne
               Altherfirst hys purpos for to wynne
               Al thys Pandare / in hys hert thought
               
                  And cast hys werk ful wysely or he wrought
            
            
               But Troylus tho / lay no lenger doun
               But vp anon vpon hys steed bay
               
                  And in the feld he pleyeth the lyoun
               Wo was the greke / that met with hym that day
               
                  And in the towne / hys manerr he holdyth ay
               So goodely he was / and gate hym so in grace
               That eche hym loued / that lokid in hys face
            
            
               
               For he become / the frendlyest knyght
               The gentyllest / and eke the most fre
               The thryftyest and one the best wyght
               That in hys tyme / was or myght be
               
                  Ded were hys Iapis / and hys cruelte
               Hys hye port / and hys maner straunge
               
                  And eche of tho / gan for a vertu chaunge
            
            
               Now lete vs stynt of Troylus a stounde
               That farith lyke a man / that hurt is sore
               
                  And is somdele of akynge of hys wounde
               Y lyssed wel / but helid no del more
               
                  And as an esy pacyent / the lore
               Abydyth of hym that goth aboute hys cure
               
                  And thus be dryuyth forth hys aduenture
            
            ¶Here endeth the first booke

               OWte of thise black wawes / for to sayle

               Thys see clepe I / the tempestous matere
               Of dyspeyre / that Troylus was ynne
               For now of hope the kalendis begynne

               Thou be my spede fro this furth / and my muse
               To Ryme wel thys booke / tyl I haue do
               Me nedeth here / none other art to vse
               For why to euery louer I me excuse
               That of no sentement / I thys endyte
               But out of latyn / in to my tunge I wryte
            
            
               
               Wherfor I wyl haue / neyther thank ne blame
               Of al thys werk / but prey yow mekely
               Dysblameth me / yf ony word be lame

               Eke though I speke / of loue vnfelyngly
               No wonder is / for it of thyng now new is
               A blynd man can not wel Iuge in hewis

               In vysityng in forme / or sayd our sawes
               For why men seyn / eche contre hath hys lawes

                  And in hys prayer / eke sawe none vnright
               
                  And for the harm / that myght eke fal more
               She gan to rewe / and dred hyr wonder sore
            
            
               
                  And thought thus vnhappis fallen thyk
               Alday for loue / in suche maner caas
               As men ben cruel / in hem self and wyk
               
                  And yf thys man sle hym self alas
               In my presence / if wyl be no solas
               What men wyl it deme / I can not sey
               It nedyth me / ful wysely to pley
            
            
               
                  And with a sorowful syke / she sayd thry
               A lord what me is tyd / a sory chaunce
               For myn estate lyeth in Iuparty
               
                  And eke myn Eames lyf / lyth in balaunce
               But natheles / wyth goddis gouernaunce
               I shal so do / myn honour shal I kepe
               
                  And eke hys lyf / and stynt for to wepe
            
            
               Of harmes two / the lasse is for to chese
               Yit had I leuer / make hym good chere
               In honour than myn owne / eames lyf to leese
               Ye sey ye nothyng / ellis requere
               Nowis quod he / myn owne nece dere
               Now wel quod she / and I wyl do my peyne
               I shal myn hert / ageynst my lust constrayne
            
            
               But that I nyl not / holdyn hym in honde
               Ne loue a man / ne can I not ne may
               Ageynst hys wyl / but ellis wyl I fonde
               Myn honour saue / please hym from day to day
               Therto nold I not oones / haue sayd nay
               But that I drede / as in hys fantasy
               But cease the cause / cesith the malady
            
            
               
               But here I make a protestacion
               That in thys proces / or ye further go
               That certaynly / for no saluacion
               Of yow though that ye sterue both two
               
                  And al the world on a day / be my fooo
               Ne shal I neuer of hym / haue other rowth
               I graunt wel quod Pandare / by my trowth
            
            
               But may I trust wel to yow / quod he
               That of thys thyng / that ye haue hyght me here
               Ye wyl holden trewly / vnto me
               Ye doute it not quod she my vncle dere
               Ne that I shal haue cause in thys matrre
               
                  Quod he to pleyne / or ofter yow to preche
               Why no parde what nedyth more speche
            
            
               Tho fyllen they / in other talis glade
               Tyl at the last / o goode Eame quod she tho
               For hys loue / whyche vs both made
               Tel me how fyrst / ye wysten of hys woo
               Wote none of it but ye / he sayd no
               Can he wel speke of loue / quod she I yow prey
               Tel me for I the bet / shal me pouruey

               Wythin the gardyn paleys / by a welle
               Gan he and I / half a day to dwelle
               Ryght for to speke / of an ordynaunce
               How we the Grekis myght dysauaunce

               So fressh so yong / so worthy semyd he
               It was an heuen / vpon hym to see

               For in and out / he is the worthyest
               Saue only Hector / whyche that is the best

               Lo suche is loue / and eke myn auenture
            
            
               Ne me to loue / a wonder is it nought
               For wel wote I my self / so god me spede
               Al wold I that noman wyst / of thys thought
               I am one the fayrest / wythouten drede
               
                  And godelyest / who so takith heede
               
                  And so men seyn / in al the towne of Troye
               What wonder is / though he of me haue Ioye

               Ryght yong and stond vntyed / in lusty lease
               Wythouth Ialowsy / or suche debate

               Or maysterful / or louen nouelrye

               Vpon thys knyght / that is the worthyest

               By al ryght / it may do me no shame

               Ful sharp begynnyng / brekyth oft at ende

               She sayd that to sleepe / wel hyr leste
               Hyr wymmen soone / in to her bed byr brought

               Of alle thyse thynges / the maner and the guyse
               To reherce it nedyth not / for ye ben wyse

               That herkeneth she / so long in goode entent

               Ne myght me so gladdyn / lo my hert

               Thou mayst answere / abyde abyde but he
               That hangyth by the neck / sooth to seyne
               In grete dysease / abydyth for the peyne

               For I haue do thy lust / wyth al my myght

               On me is not a long / thyn euyl fare

               Now help thy self / and let for no slouth

               To take it / to haue of hym rowth
               In harmyng of my self / or repreue
               Bere it ageyn / for hym that ye on leeue

               Yf for the citee / whyche that stondyth yondyr

               To harm of yow / what lust ye thys to make

                  And Pandarus sawe hys woodely peyne
               Wax wele ny deed / for rowth sooth to seyne
               
                  And besily wyth al hys hert he cast
               Som̄e of hys woo to slee / and that as fast
            
            
               
               
                  And sayd lord / and frend / and brother dere
               
                  God wote that thy desease / doeth me woo
               But wylt thou stynt / al thys woful chere
               
                  And by my trouth / or it be dayes two
               
                  And god to forn / yit shal I shape it so
               That thou shalt come / in to a certeyn place
               Ther as thou mayst thy self / prey hyr of grace
            
            
               
                  And certaynly I note / yf thou it wost
               But tho that ben expert / in loue I sey
               It is one of the thynges / that furtherith most
               A man to haue a leyser / for to prey
               
                  And siker place hys woo for to bewrey
               For in good hert / ther must rowth impresse
               To hyr that seeth / the gyltles in dystresse
            
            
               Perauenture thynkest thou / though it be soo
               That kynd wold done / for to begynne
               To haue a maner rowth / vpon my woo
               Seyth daūgyer nay thou shalt me neuer wynne
               In that maner for no maner gynne
               Though that she bende yit / she stant on Roote
               What in effect is thys / vnto my boote
            
            
               Than ther ageynst / whan that the sturdy oke
               On whyche men hacke / oft for the nones
               
                  Receyued hath / the happy fallynge stroke
               The grete sweyght / doth it falle at ones
               As don thyse rokkes / to the mylstones
               For swyfter cours / comyth thyng of weyght
               Whan it descendyth / than don thynges 
                     ••
                  ght
            
            
               But Reede that bowyth doun / wyth euery blast
               Ful lyghtly wyth the wynd / it wyl aryse
               But so nyl not an oke / whan it is cast
               It nedyth me not / the long to deuyse
               Men shuld reioyse / of grete empryse
               Acheuyth wele / and stondyth oute of doute
               Al haue men ben / the lenger ther aboute
            
            
               
               But Troylus now tel me yf the lest
               A thyng the whyche / I shal aske the
               Whyche is the brother / that thou louest best
               As in thy veray hertis pryuyte
               Ywys my dere brother / Deyphebe
               Now quod Pandare / or houris twyes twelue
               He shal the ease / vnwyst of hym selue
            
            
               Now lete me alone / and werke as I may
               
                  Quod he / and to deyphebus wente he tho
               Whyche had hys lord / and grete frend ben ay
               Saue Troylus noman he loued so
               To tel in short / wythout wordis mo
               
                  Quod Pandarus / I pray yow that ye be
               
                  Frend to a cause / whyche that touchyeth me
            
            
               Yis parde quod Deyphebus / wel thou wost
               In alle that euer I may / and god to fore
               Al neere it but for oo man / that I loue most
               My brother Troylus / but sey me wherfore
               It is for sith the day / that I was bore
               I nas nor neuermore / to be I thynk
               Ageynst a thyng / that myght the forthynk
            
            
               Pandarus gan hym thank / and thus he seyde
               Lo sire I haue a lady in thys towne
               That is my neece / and callyd is Criseyde
               Whyche som̄e men wolde do oppression
               
                  And wrongfully haue her possession
               Wherfor yowre lordshyp / I yow beseche
               To be oure frend wythout more speche
            
            
               Deiphebus answerd / is it thys
               That thou to me spack of / so straungely
               Criseyde my frend / he sayd she is
               Than nedyth quod Deiphebus / hardily
               Nomore of thys for trusteth wel that I
               Wyl be hyr champioun / wyth spere and swerd
               
               I rought not / though all hyr foes it herd
               
            
            
               
               But tel me / for thou wost thys matere
               I myght hyr best auayle / now late see
               
                  Quod Pandarus / yf ye my lord so dere
               
                  Wold as now do / thys honour vnto me
               To prayen hyr thys / to morow that she
               Come vnto yow / hyr playntes to deuyse
               Hyr aduersaryes / wold therof agryse
            
            
               
                  Lord yf that more / I durst yow prey as now
               
                  And charge yow to haue so grete trauayle
               To haue som̄e of yowre brethern / here with yow
               Than myght hyr cause / the better auayle
               Than wote I wel / she myght neuer fayle
               For to be holp / what at your instaunce
               What wyth hyr othyr frendes / sustenaunce
            
            
               Deiphebus whyche that was / come of kynde
               To al honour / and bounte to consent
               
                  Answerd it shal be don / and I can fynde
               Yit gretter help to thys / in myn entent
               That wylt thou sey / yf for Heleyne I sent
               To speke of thys / I trow it be best
               For she may leede Paris / as hyr lest
            
            
               For Hector whyche that is my lord my brother
               It nedyth not to pray hym frend to be
               For I haue herd hym / bothe one tyme and other
               Speke of Criseyde suche honour that he
               May sey no bet / suche hap to hym hath she
               So nedyth not hys help / now for to craue
               He shal be suche / ryght as we wyl hym haue
            
            
               Speke thou thy self also to Troylus
               On my behalue / and pray hym wyth vs dyne
               Syr al thys shal be do / quod Pandarus
               
                  And toke hys leue / and neuer gan to fyne
               But to hys neecis hous / as streyght as a lyne
               He come and fond hyr / from the mete aryse
               
                  And set hym doun / & spack right in thys wyse
            
            
               
               He sayd / O veray god so haue I ronne
               Lo neece myn / see ye not how I swete
               I note whether the more / ye me thank conne
               Be ye not ware / how fals Poliphete
               Is now aboute / eftsoones to plete
               To bryng on yow / aduocatis newe
               I no quod she / and chaungyd all her hewe
            
            
               What is he more aboute / me to dretche
               
                  And do me wrong / what shal I do alas
               Yit of hym self / nothyng wold I retche
               Ner it for Anthenor and Eneas
               That ben hys frendes / in suche maner cas
               But for the loue of god / myn vncle dere
               No fors of it / lete hym haue al yfere
            
            
               Wythout that I haue ynowgh for vs
               Nay quod Pandare / it shal nothyng be soo
               For I haue be right now / wyth Deiphebus
               At Hector / and myn other lordis moo
               
                  And shortly made eche of theym / hys foo
               That by my thryft / he shal it neuer wynne
               For aught he can / whan so that he begynne
            
            
               
                  And as they cast / what was best to done
               Deiphebus / of hys owne curtesye
               Came hyr to prey / in hys owne propyr persone
               To hold hym / on the morow companye
               At dyner whyche she wold / hym not denye
               But goodely gan / to hys prayer obeye
               He thankyth hyr / and went vpon hys weye
            
            
               Whan thys was done thys pandare vp anone
               To tel in short / forth he gan to wende
               To Troylus as styl as ony stone
               Of al thys thyng he told hym word and ende
               
                  And how he Deiphebus gan to blende
               
                  And sayd now is tyme / yf that thou conne
               Bere the wele to morow / and al is wonne
            
            
               
               Now speke now prey / now pytously compleyne
               Leue not for nyce shame / or drede or slowth
               Somtyme a man mote / tel hys owne peyne
               Byleue it and she wyl haue / on the rowth
               Thou shalt be sauyd / by thy feyth in trowth
               But wele wote I thou art in a drede
               
                  And what it is / lo I can it rede
            
            
               Thou thynkest now / how shal I do al thys
               For by my chere / must folke espye
               That for loue is / that I fare amys
               Yit had I leuer ywys / for sorow dye
               Now thynk not so / thou doest grete folye
               For I ryght now / haue found a manere
               Of sleyght / for to couere al thy chyere
            
            
               Thou shalt goo ouer nyght / and that as blyue
               Vnto Deiphebus hous / the to pley
               Thy malady the bet / awey to dryue
               For why thou semyst syke / the sooth to sey
               Soone after that / doun in thy bed the ley
               
                  And sey thou mayst / no lenger vp endure
               
                  And be right there / and byde thy aueuture
            
            
               Sey that the feuer / is wont the to take
               The same tyme / and last tyl a morowe
               
                  And lete see now / how wel thou kanst it make
               For parde sike is he that is in sorowe
               Go now fare wele / and venus here to borowe
               I hope and thou / thy pourpos hold ferme
               In grace she shal / the fully conferme
            
            
               
                  Quod Troylus ywys / thou nedeles
               Counseylest me / sikerly to feyne
               For I am sike / in ernest douteles
               So wel ny that / I sterue for the peyne
               
                  Quod Pandarus / thou shalt the bettyr pleyne
               
                  And hast the lasse nede / to countrefete
               For hym men deme hote / that men see swete
            
            
               
               Lo hold the at thy Trist clos / and I
               Shal wele the dere / vnto thy lowe dryue
               Therwyth he toke hys leue / al softly
               And Troylus to paleys went blyue
               So glad he nas / neuer in all hys lyue
               
                  And to Pandarus rede / gan al assent
               
                  And to Deiphebus hous / at nyght he went
            
            
               What nedyth yow / to tellen of the chere
               That Deiphebus gan hys brothyr make
               Or hys accesse / or hys sikely manere
               How men hym gan / wyth clothys lade
               Whan he was leyde / & how men did hym glade
               But alle for nought / he held forth hys guyse
               As ye haue herd / Pandare hym deuyse
            
            
               But certeyne is / or Troylus hym leyde
               Deiphebus preyd hym / ouer nyght
               To be a frend and helpyng to Criseyde
               
                  God wote that he / it graunted anon right
               To be hyr ful frend / wyth al hys myght
               But suche a nede it was / to praye hym thenne
               As for to bydde / a woode man to renne
            
            
               The morowe come / and nyghen gan the tyme
               Of mele tyde / that the fayre quene heleyne
               Shoope hyr to be / an hour after the pryme
               Wyth deiphebus / to whom she wold not feyne
               But as hys suster / homely soth to seyne
               She come to dyner / in hyr playn entent
               But god & Pādare / wyst none what this ment
            
            
               Come eke Criseyde al innocent of thys
               Antygone hyr suster and Targe also
               But fle we now prolixite best is
               For loue of god and lete vs fast goo
               Ryght to theffect / wythout talis moo
               Why al thys folk / assembled in that place
               
                  And lete vs of theyr salowynges pace
            
            
               
               Grete honour dyd hem Deiphebus certeyne
               And fed hem wel / with al yt myght hem lyke
               But euermore alas / was hys refreyne
               My good brother / Troylus the sike
               Lyeth yet / and therwyth al he gan to sike
               
                  And after that / he peyned hym to glade
               Hem as he myght / and good chere hem made
            
            
               
                  Compleyned eke Heleyne / of hys sikenesse
               So feythfully / that pyte was to here
               
                  And euery wyght than / was for that accesse
               A leche anon / and seyde in thys manere
               Men curen folke / thys charme I wyl yow

               But ther sat one / al lyst her not to

               That thought / yit best cowd I be hys lec

               After compleynt / than gan they hym to preyse
               As folk don yet / when som̄e han bygonne
               To preyse a man / and vp wyth hym to reyse
               A thousand fold / yit hyer than the sonne
               He is that can / that fewe lordis conne
               
                  And Pandarus of that / they wold afferme
               He not forgate / hys praysyng to conferme
            
            
               
                  Herd al thys / Cryseyde wel ynowgh
               
                  And euery word / gan to notyfye
               For whyche wyth sobre chere / her hert lowgh
               For who is that / nold hym gloryfye
               To mone suche a knyght / to lyue or dye
               But al passe I / lese ye to long dwelle
               For al is / for a fyne that I you telle

               To speke here of the needis / of Criseyde
            
            
               
               Heleyne whyche that / by the hand hyr held
               
               Toke fyrst the tale / and sayd gowe blyue
               
                  And goodly on Criseyde she beheld

               That doeth yow harm / & bryng hym self of lyue
               
                  And yeue me sorowe / but he shal it rewe
               Yf that I may / and alle folkes be trewe
            
            
               Tel thou thy neecis caas / quod Deiphebus
               To Pandarus / for thou canst best it telle
               My lordis and my ladyes it stant thus
               What shuld I lenger / do yow dwelle
               He rong hym out a proces lyke a belle
               Vpon hyr foo / that hyght poliphete
               So haynous that men / myght on it spete
            
            
               
                  Answerd of this eche of theym / worse thā other
               
                  And poliphete / thus gan they waryen
               An hanged lo such one / were he my brother
               
                  And so it shal / for it may not varien
               What shuld I lenger / in thys processe taryen
               Playnly al at ones / they hyr behyght
               To be hyr frend / in all that euer they myght
            
            
               Spack than heleyne / and herd Pandarus
               Wote ought my lord my brother thys matere
               I meane Hector / or wote it Troylus
               He sayd ye / but wyl ye now me here
               Me thynketh thys / sith Troylus is here
               It were goode / yf that ye wolde assent
               She told hym her self / al thys or she went
            
            
               For he wyl haue the more / hyr grief at hert
               By cause loo / that she a lady is
               
                  And by yowre leue / I wyl but in stert
               
                  And do yow wyte / and that anon ywys
               Yf that he sleepe / or wyl ought here of thys
               
                  And in he leepe / and sayd hym in hys eere
               
                  God haue thy soule brought I haue thy bere
            
            
               
               To smylen gan / of thys Troylus
               
                  And Pandarus / wythout restonyng

                  And seyd hem so / ther be no taryeng

               As she best cowde / of sorow hym to comfort
            
            
               
               Soone after quod she / we yow byseke
               My dere brother Deiphebus / and I
               For loue of god / and so doth Pandare eke
               To be good lord / and frend right hertyly
               Vnto Criseyde whyche that certeynly
               Receyuyth wrong / as wote wel here Pandare
               That can hyr cas / wel bet than I declare
            
            
               Thys Pandarus / gan now hys tunge affyle

               Whan it was seyd / soone after in a whyle
               
                  Quod Troylus / as soone as I may gon
               I wyl ryght fayn / wyth al my myght anon
               Haue god my trowth / hyr cause to sustene
               Goode thryft haue ye / quod Heleyne the quene
            
            
               
                  Quod Pandadas / and yit yowre wyl be
               That she may take hyr leue / or that she go
               Now ellis god forbede it tho quod she
               Yf that she vouchesauf / for to do so
               
                  And wyth that word / quod Troylus ye two
               Deiphebe / and ye my suster dere
               To yow haue I to speke / of a matere
            
            
               To be aduysed / by yowre aduyse the bettir
               
                  And had as hap was / at hys beddis hede
               The copy of a tretice / and a lettyr
               That Hector had hym sent / to askyn rede
               Yf suche a man / were worthy to be dede
               Note I not who / but in a grysely wyse
               He prayed hem bothe anon / on hyt auyse
            
            
               Deiphebus / gan thys lettyr vnfold
               
               In ernest grete / so dyde heleyne the qwene
               
                  And romyng outward / fast gan it behold
               
               
                  Dounward a stayre / and in to an herber grene
               Thys ylke thyng / they redden hem betwene
               
                  And largely / the montenaunce of an honre
               They gonne on it / for to rede and powre
            
            
               
               Now lete hem rede / and tourne we anon
               To Pandarus / that gan ful fast pry
               That as wel in and out / gan he gon
               Vnto the chambre a loft / and that on hy
               
                  And sayd god saue al thys company
               Come now my neede / my lady awene Heleyne
               Abydyth yow / and eke my lordis

                  weyne

               Or whom ye lyst / or nofors hardyly
               The lesse preace the bet / come forth wyth me

               Hem al thre / and whan ye may goodely
               Yowre tyme see / takyth of hem yowre leue
               Lest we to long / hys rest hym byreue

               Styntyth ryght here / and softely ye pley

                     •
                  r one is / god hym amende

               On hys half / whyche that vs soule hath sende
               
                  And in the vertu / of the corownes tweyne
               Sle not this man / that hath for yow this peyne
            
            
               Fy on the deuyl / thynk whyche one be is

               Thynk al suche taryed tyde / lost is
               That wyl ye both sey / whan ye ben one
               
                  And sikerly ther yit / dyuyneth none
               Vpon yow two / come of now yf ye conne
               Whyle folk is blent / lo al the tyme is wonne
            
            
               
               In tyteryng in pursuyte / and delayes
               Folk wyl dyuyne / at waggyng of a stre
               That though ye wold / haue after merye dayes
               Than dare ye not for why / for he and he
               Spack suche a word / thus lookid she and she
               Thus tyme y lost / I dare not wyth yow dele
               Come of therfor / and bryng hym to hys hele
            
            
               But now to yow / ye louers that ben here
               Was not trroylus / in a cankerdort
               That lay & myght / the whyspryng of her here
               
                  And thought o lord / now rennyth my sort
               Fully to dye / or haue no comfort
               
                  And was the fyrst tyme he shuld hyr preye
               Of loue / o myghty god what shal I seye

            ¶And here begynneth the prologe of
the thyrde booke
            
               O Blisful light of which the beames clere
               Adourneth / al the hye heuenes fayre
               O sonnys lyf / O Iouys doughter d
                     •
                  re
               Pbe saunce o loue / o goodely debonayre
               In gentyl hertis / redy to repayre
               O veray cause of hele / and of gladnesse
               Y heryed be thy myght / and thy goodnesse
            
            
               In heuene and helle / erthe and see
               Is fyrst thy myght / yf that I wel dyscerne
               As man bryd best / fyssh herbe and grene tree
               The feld in tymes / wyth vapour eterne
               
                  God louyth and to loue / he wyl not werne
               
                  And in thys world / no lyues creature
               Wythout loue is worth / or may endure
            
            
               
               In Iouis fyrst / to thylk effectis glade
               Thurgh whyche that thynges / lyuen al and be
               
                  Commendyd / and amoureux hem made
               O mortal thyng / and as thou lyst ay see
               Yaue hem in loue / ease or aduersite
               
                  And in a thousand fourmes / doun hem sent
               To loue in erthe / and whom ye lyst is blent
            
            
               The fyers Mars / to apesyn of hys Ire
               
                  And as ye lyst me make hertis dygne
               Algatis hem / that ye wyl sette a fyre
               That dreden shame / and vyces yit resigne
               Ye to hem curteys / fressh be and benygne
               
                  And hem promotith / aftyr a wyght entendyth
               The Ioye that he hath / your myght hym fendyth
            
            
               Ye holdyn regne and hous / in vnyte
               The sothfast cause / and frendshyp be also
               Ye know all thylk / couered qualyte
               Of thynges whiche that folkes wondren on so
               That they can not constrewe / how it may geo
               She louyth hym / or why loueth he not here
               Or why this fissh / & not that comyth to the were
            
            
               The folke a lawe / han sette in vniuers
               
                  And thys know I / by theym that louers be
               That who so striuyth with yow / hath the wers
               Now lady bryght / for thy benygnyte
               At reuerence of hem / that seruen the
               Whos clerk I am / teche me deuyse
               Som̄e Ioye of that / is felt in thy seruyse
            
            
               Ye in my naked / hertis sentement
               In elde / and do me shewe of thy wytnesse
               Caliope / thy dayes ben now present
               For now is nede / seest thon not my dystresse
               How I must telle anon / right the gladnesse
               Of Troylus to venus heryeng
               
               To which gladnesse who nede hath god hym bryng
               
            
            
               ¶Here endeth the prologe
         
         
            ¶And here begynneth the thyrde booke
            
               LAy al thys mene whyle Troylus
               
                  Recordyng hys lesson / in thys manere
               Mafey thought he / thus wil I sey & thus
               Thus wyl I pleyne / vnto my lady dere
               That word is good / & that shal be my matere
               Thys wyl I not for geten / in no wyse

               Come soupe wyth hym / at hys house at eue

               He wold neuer come / there as she were
            
            
               
               
                  And she ageyn / gan hym for to rowne
               
                  And asked hym / yf Troylus were there
               He swore hyr nay / for he was out of towne
               
                  And sayd neece / I pose that he were there
               Ye durst neuer haue / the more fere
               For rather than men / shuld hym espye
               
               Me were leuer / a thousand fold to dye
            
            
               Nat lyst myn Auctour / fully to declaryn
               What that she thought / whan he sayd so
               That Troylus was / out of towne y faryn
               As yf he sayd / soth therof or no
               But that she grauntyd / wyth hym for to go
               Wythout nayeng / sith he her besought
               
                  And as hys neece / obeyed as hyr ought

               Al though wyth hym to go / was no fere
               For to be ware / of gostly peoples speche
               That dremen thynges / whyche that neuer were

               Looke al be wel / for I do as yow lyst

               For neece thys is yowre owne hous parde
               Now be myry I sey / it is now no game
               To wende now home / it were to me a shame

               Were it a game / or sooth for to telle
               I am now glad / syth that ye lyst dwelle

               By god right in my lytel closet yonder

               By wardeyn / of your wymmen euerychone

               And carith not for the wedir / though it be aloft
               The wyne was brought / & whan so that you lest
               Than is it tyme / for to go to rest

               More in the place / out of the chambre gone

               That whom ye lyst of hem / ye may soone calle

               A bed were they / as I haue yow seyde
               Thys was nomore / to skippe ne to traunce

               Yf ony man was stiryng / ony where
               
                  And lete theym sleepe / that a bed were

               For therwyth mene I / fynally the peyne
               That holt your hert / and myn in heuynesse
               Fully to slene / and euery wrong redresse
            
            
               My good hert not I / for why ne how
               That Ialowsye alas / that wyckid wyuere
               So causeles is cropen / in to yow
               The harm of whyche / I wold fayne delyuere
               Alas that ye al hool / or of hym a shyuere
               
                  Shuld haue hys refute / in so dygne a place
               That Ioue out soone / out of your hert hym race
            
            
               But o thou Ioue / auctour of nature
               Is thys an hononr / vnto thy deyte
               That folk vngylty / suffre here Iniure
               
                  And he that gylty is / vnquyt goth he
               O were it leeful / for to pleyne / on the
               That vndeserued / suffrist Ialowsye
               Of that I wold / vpon the pleyne and crye
            
            
               
               Eke al my woo is thys / that men now vsen
               To seye ryght thus / that Ialowsye is loue
               
                  And wold a busshel of venym all excusen
               For that one greyn of loue / is in shoue
               But that wote the hye god / that sit aboue
               Yf it be syker loue / hate or grame
               
                  And after that / it ought to bere hys name
            
            
               But certeyn is / som̄e maner Ialowsye
               Is excusable / more than som̄e ywys
               As whan cause / and som̄e suche fantasye
               Wyth pyte so wel / repressid is
               That it vnneth doeth / or sayth amys
               But goodely drynkyth vp / all hys dystresse
               
                  And that excuse I / for the gentylnesse
            
            
               
                  And som̄e so ful / of furye and dyspyte
               That it surmountyth / hys repressioun
               But hert myn / ye be not in thys plyte
               That thank I god / for whyche your passioun
               I wyl not calle it but an Illusioun
               Of habundaunce of loue / and besy cure
               That doeth your hert / thys dysease endure
            
            
               Of whyche I am ryght sory / but not wroth
               But for my desire / and your hertis rest
               Whether so yow lyst / by ordal or by oth
               By sort or be what wyse / so that yow lest
               For loue of god / late preue it for the best
               
                  And yf that I be gylty do me deye
               Alas what myght I more / done or seye
            
            
               Wyth that a fewe / bryght teeris newe
               Out of hyr eyen fyl / and thus she seyde
               Now god thou wost / in thought ne dede vntrewe
               To Troylus was neuer yit Criseyde
               Wyth that hyr hond / doun in the bed she leyde
               
                  And wyth the shete it wryed / and sighed sore
               
                  And held hyr pees / not a word spack she more
            
            
               
               But now help god / to qwenche al thys sorow
               So hope I that he shal / for he best may
               For I haue seen / a ful mysty morow
               Folowe ful oft / a myry somer day
               
                  And after wynter foloweth grene may
               Men seen alday / and rede eke in storyes
               That after sharp showres / ben vyctoryes
            
            
               Thys Troylus / whan he hyr wordis herd
               
               Haue ye no care / hym lyst not to slepe
               For it thought hym / no strokes of a yerd
               
               To here or see / Criseyde hys lady wepe
               But wele he felt / aboute hys hert crepe
               For euery teere / whyche that Criseyde as
                     •
                  ert
               The cramp of doth / streyneth hym by the hert
            
            
               
                  And in hys mynd / he gan the tyme acurse
               That he came there / or that he was bore
               For now is wycke / tornyd in to worse
               
                  And al the labour / he hath do byfore
               He thought it lost / he wend he nas but lore
               O Pandarus alas thought he / thy wyle
               Seruyth of nought / so welawey the whyle

               Nay dere hert myn / quod he ywys

               Foryeue it me / myn owne swete hert
            
            
               
               Tho Troylus wyth bus / of that supprysed
               
               Put all in goddis hond / as he that ment
               
                  Nothyng but wel / and sodaynly auysed
               
               He hyr in armes / fast to hym hent
               
                  And Pandarus / wyth ful goode entent
               Layde hym to sleepe / and sayd yf ye be wyse
               Swowne not now / lest mo folke aryse
            
            
               What myght or may / the sely lark sey
               Whan that the sperhawke / hath it in hys foote
               I can nomore / but of thys ylke twey
               To whom thys tale / sugre he or swoote
               Though that I tarye a yere / som̄tyme I mote
               After myn auctour / tel of theyr gladnesse
               As wele as I haue / told theyr heuynesse
            
            
               Criseyde wyth that / felt hyr thus y take
               As wryten clerkis / in theyr bookes old
               
               Ryght as an aspen leef / she gan to quake
               Whan she hyr felt / in hys armes fold
               
               
                  And Troylus al hool / of hys cares cold
               
               Gan thankyn tho / the bryght goddis seuene
               That sundry peynes / bryngen folk to heuene
            
            
               Thys Troylus in armes gan hyr streyne
               
                  And sayd o swete / as euer mote I gone
               Now be ye caught / ther nys but we tweyne
               Now yeldyth yow / for other boote is none
               To that Criseyde / answerd thus anone
               Ne had I er now / my swete hert dere
               Be yolden ywys / I were not now here
            
            
               O sooth is sayde / that helyd for to be
               As of a feuer / or another grete sikenesse
               Men must drynk alday / as men may see
               Ful bytter drynk / and for to haue gladnesse
               Men duren of peyne / and grete dystresse
               I meane it here / as of thys aduenture
               That thurgh a peyne / hath found now hys cure
            
            
               
               
                  And now swetnesse / semyth more swete
               That bytternesse assayed / was byforn
               For out of woo / in blysse now they fleete
               None suche they felt / sith that they were born
               Now is thys bet / than both two be lorn
               For loue of god / take euery womman heede
               To worke thus / whan it comyth to neede

               Whan she hys trowth / and clene entent wyst

                  And next Ymeneus / I the grete
               For neuer man was / to yow goddis hold
               
               As I that ye haue / brought from cares cold
               
            
            
               Benygne loue / thou holy bonde of thynges
               Who so wyl grace / and lyst not the honoure
               Lo hys desire wyl fle / wythout wynges
               For thou noldyst of bounte / hem socoure
               That seruen best / and alwey most laboure
               But yf thy grace / passed our desertis
               Al were lost / that I dare sey certis
            
            
               
                  And for thow me / that cowd best deserue
               Of hem that nombred be vnto thy grace
               Hast holpen there / I lykly was to sterue
               
                  And me bystowed / in so hygh a place
               That ilke boundis / may no blis pace
               I can nomore / but lawde and reuerence
               Be to thy bounte / and thyn excellence
            
            
               
                  And ther wythal / Criseyde anon he kyst
               Of whyche certeyn / she felt no dysease

               Myn hert swete / how I myght yow please
               What man quod he / was euer thus at ease
               As I on whom / the fayrest and the best
               That euer I say / deyneth hyr hert to rest
            
            
               Here may men see / that mercy passyth right
               Thexperience of thys / is felt in me

               So thynkyth though I vnworthy be
               Yit mote neede / amende in som̄e wyse
               Ryght thurgh the vertu / of yowre hye seruyse

               O nyght alas why nyl thou / ouer vs houe

               Wele ought bestis pleyne / and folk the chyde
               That ther as day / wyth labour wold vs brest
               That thou vs fleest / and late vs haue no rest
            
            
               Thou doest alas / to shortly thyn offyce

               For thurgh the rakel hyeng out of Troye
               Haue I forgo / thus hastyly my Ioye

               Now torne we ageyne / to Troylus
               That restles / ful long abed lay
               
                  And pryuely sent after Pandarus
               To hym to come / in all the hast he may
               He come anone not ones seyd he nay
               
                  And Troylus / ful sobyrly hym grette
               
                  And doun on hys beddis side hym sette
            
            
               Thys Troylus / wyth all the affection
               Of frendly loue / that hert may deuyse
               To Pandarus / on knees fyl a doun
               
                  And or that he wold / of that place aryse
               He gan hym thank / in the best wyse
               A thowsand tymes / and gan the day to blesse
               That he was born / to bryng hym from dystresse
            
            
               
                  And sayd o frende / of frendis altherbest
               That euer was the sooth for to telle
               Thou hast in heuene / brought my sowle at rest
               Fro Cochita / the fyry flood of helle
               
                  And though I myght / a thousand tymes selle
               Vpon a day / my lyf in thy seruyse
               It myght not amounte / ne in that suffyse
            
            
               
               The sonne whyche that al the world may see
               Was neuer yit my lyf / dare I sey
               So inly fayre / so goodely as is she
               Whos I am and shal / tyl that I deye
               
                  And that I thus am here / I dare wel seye
               That thankyd be the hye worthynesse
               Of loue and eke / thy kynde besynesse
            
            
               Thus hast thou me / not a lytel yeue
               For whyche oblyged be / to the for ay
               My lyf for why / for thurgh thy help I lyue
               Or ellis ded had I be / gon many a day
               
                  And wyth that word / doun in hys bed he lay
               
                  And Pandarus / ful sobyrly hym herd
               
               Tyl al was seyde / and than he thus answerd
               
            
            
               My dere frend / yf I haue do for the
               In ony caas / god wote it is me lyef
               
                  And am as glad / as man of it may
               
                  God help me so / but take it not agryef
               For loue of god / beware of thys meschyef
               That ther as now / brought art to thy blisse
               That thou thy self / ne cause it not to mysse
            
            
               For of fortunes sharp aduersyte
               The worst kynde of infortune is thys
               A man to haue be in prosperyte
               
                  And it remembre / whan it passid is
               Thou art wyse ynow / for why do not amys
               Be not to rakel / though thou sitte warme
               For yf thou do / certeyne it wyl the harme
            
            
               Thou art at ease / hold the now therin
               For al so sure / as redy ys euer fyre
               As grete a craft is / to kepe wel as wyn
               Brydle thy speche / and thy desire
               For worldly Ioye / holt not but by a wyre
               That preuyth wel / it brest alwey so oft
               For thy neede is / to worche wyle it is soft

               For eche of hem / gan others lust obey
               Felicyte whyche that these clerkis wyse
               Commendyn so / ne may not here suffyse
               Thys Ioy may not / wryten be wyth ynk
               It passyth al that / ony hert may thynk
            
            
               But cruel day / so welaway the stounde
               Gan for to approche / as they be signes knew
               For whyche hem thought / feelen dethis wound
               
               So woo was hem / that chaungen gan theyr hew
               
                  And they bygan / to dyspyse al new
               Callynge it traytour enuyous and wors
               
                  And byttyrly the day lyght they curs
            
            
               
                  Quod Troylus alas / now am I ware
               That Pierers / and the swyft styedis thre
               Whyche that drawen forth / the sonnes chare
               Han gon som̄e bypath / in dyspyte of me
               That makyth it so soone / day to be
               
                  And for the sonne / hastyth hym thus to ryse
               Ne shal I neuer do efte hym sacryfyse
            
            
               
               But needis day / departe must hem soone
               
                  And whan theyr speche doon was / & theyr chere
               They twynne anon / as they be wont to done
               
                  And setten tyme / of metyng eft in feere
               And many a nyght they wrouht in this manere
               
                  And thus fortune / a tyme lad hem in Ioye
               Criseyde and eke / the kynges sone of Troye
            
            
               In suffysaunce / in blys / and in syngynges
               Thus Troylus gan al hys lyf to lede
               He spendyth Iustyth / and makyth festynges
               He yeuyth frely oft / and chaungyth weede
               
                  And holt aboute hym / ay wythoute drede
               A world of folk / as cam hym wel of kynde
               The fresshest and the best / that he cowde fynde
            
            
               That suche a voys of hym / was and a steuene
               Thurgh out the world / of honour and largesse
               That it vp rong / to the yate of heuene
               
                  And as in loue / he was in suche gladnesse
               That in hys hert / he demyth as I gesse
               That ther nys louer / in thys world at ease
               So wel as he / and thus gan loue hym please
            
            
               The goodely hed & bounte / whyche that kynde
               In ony other lady / had y set
               Can not the mountenaunce / of a knot vnbynde
               About hys hert / of al Criseydes net
               He was so narow / masked and y knet
               That it to vndo / on ony maner syde
               That wyl not be / for aught that may betyde
            
            
               
                  And by the hond / ful oft he wold take
               Thys pandarus / and in to the gardyn leede
               
                  And suche a fest / and suche a proces make
               Hym of Criseyde / and of hyr wommanheede
               
                  And of hyr beaute / eke wythouten drede
               It was an heuene / hys wordis for to here
               
                  And than he wold syng / in thys manere
            
            
               
               Loue that of erth & see / hath in gouernaunce
               Loue that hys hestis / hath in heuenes hye
               Loue that wyth / an holsum alyaunce
               Holt peoples Ioyned as he lest hem gye
               Loue that endueth / lawe of companye
               
                  And cowples doeth / in vertu for to dwelle
               
                  Bynd thys accord / that I haue told & telle
            
            
               That / that the world / wyth feyth that is stable
               Dyuersith so hys stoundis / concordyng
               
               That Elementis / that ben so dyscordable
               Holt in a bonde perpetuelly duryng
               
               That Phebus must / hys rosy day forth bryng
               
               
                  And the moone haue lordship ouer the nyghtis
               Al thys doth Loue al / heryed be hys myghtis
            
            
               That that the see / gredy is to flowyn
               Constreyneth / to a certeyn ende so
               As floodes that so fresshly / they ne growyn
               To drenche the erthe / and al for euermo
               
                  And yf that loue ought let / hys brydel go
               
                  And that now lyuyth / a sundre shold kepe
               
                  And lost were al / that loue now holt to hepe
