               So serchen hertis al / and fast bynd
               
               That from his bond / no wight out ye wey wyst

               To make hem loue / and that hem lyst ay rewe
               On hertis sore / and kepe hem that ben trewe
            
            
               In al needis / for the townes werre

Here endeth the thyrd book of Troylus
         
         
            And here begynneth the prolog of the fourth
book
            
               bVt al to lytel wel awey the whyle
               Lastyth suche ioye blyssed he fortune
               That semeth trewest whan she doth begyle
               And can to fooles so hyr song entune
               That she doeth hent & blent as traitour comune
               And when a wyght is from hir whele I throw
               Than laughyth she & maketh hym a mowe
            
            
               From Troylus gan she hyr bryght face
               Awey to wrye & took of hym none hede
               But cast hym clene al oute of hyr grace
               
                  And on hyr whele she set vp Dyomede
               For whiche ryght now myn hert gynneth blede
               
                  And now my penne alas with whiche I write
               Qnaketh for drede of that I must endyte
            
            
               For how Creseyde Troylus forsoke
               Or at the lest how that she was vnkynde
               Mote be hens forth mater of my book
               As wryten folk thurgh whiche it is in mynd
               
               Alas that euer she shold cause fynde
               To speke hyr harm / & yf they on hyr lye
               Ywys hem self shal haue the vylonye
            
            
               O ye Herynes nyghtes doughters thre
               That endeles compleyne euer in peyne
               Megera Allecto and eke Thesyphone
               Thou cruel mars eke fader to Quyryne
               This ylk fourth book helpe me to fyne
               Soo that the loos & loue and lyf y fere
               Of Troylus be fully shewed here
            
            Here endeth the prologe
         
         
            
               And begynneth the fourth book
            
               
               lYggyng in hoost as I haue told

               The grekes strong about Troy toun
               Befel yt when phebus gan shyne ywis
               Vpon the brest of hercules lyoun
               That Hector with ful many a bold baroun
               Cast on a day with grekes for to fyght
               As he was wonte to greue hem yf he myght
            
            
               Note I how long or short it was bytwene
               This purpoos & that day they fyght ment
               But on a day wel bryght & sheene
               With spere in hond & bygge bowes bent
               Hector & many a worthy knyght oute went
               And in the berde anone withouten let
               Her foomen in the feld hem fast met
            
            
               The long day with speres sharp y ground
               
               With arrwes / dartes / swerdes / maces felle
               They fyght & bryng hors & man to ground
               
               And with theyr axes oute the braynes quelle
               But in the last shoure forth for to telle
               The folk of Troye hem self so mysledde
                     •
                  
               
               That with ye wors hōward at nyȝt they fledd

               But netheles a trewes was ther take
               At grekes request and tho they gan treate
               Of prysoners a chaunge for to make
               This thyng anone was couth in euery strete
               And for the surplus youen sommes grete
               Bothe in the syege & Towne & euery where
               And with the fyrst it cam to Calcas ere
            
            
               
               When Calcas knewe the treatys shold hold
               
               In concystory among grekes sone
               He gan in thryng forth with lordes old
               And set hym there as he was wonte to done
               And with theyr chaungyng he had hem a bone
               For loue of god to do that reuerence
               To stynt noyse & yeue hym audyence
            
            
               Than sayd he thus loo lordes myn I was
               Troian as it is knowe oute of drede
               And yf ye remembre I am Calcas
               That alther fyrst yaf comfort to youre nede
               And told wele how ye shold spede
               For dredeles thurgh yow shalle in a sconde
               This Troye be brent & drawen doun to grounde
            
            
               And in what fourme / & in what maner wyse
               This toune to shende / & al youre lust to ach
                     •
                  ue
               Ye haue or thys me herd wel deuyse
               This knowen ye my lordes as I leue
               And for the grekes were me so leue
               I come my self in my proper persone
               To teche in this what ye were best to done
            
            
               Hauyng vpon my tresour ne my rent
               Ryght no respect to respect of youre case
               Thus al my good I lefte & to yow went
               Wenyng in this my lordes yow to plese
               But al this losse doth me no dysese
               I vouchesauf as wysely haue I ioye
               For yow to lese al that I haue in Troye
            
            
               Sauf of a doughter that I left alas
               Slepyng at home when oute of Troye I stert
               O sterne & cruel fader that I was
               How myght I haue in that so hard an hert
               Alas I ne had brought hyr in my shert
               For sorow of which I wol not leue to morow
               But yf ye lordes rewe vpon my sorow
            
            
               
               For by that cause I sawe no tyme or now
               Hyr to delyuere hold I haue my pees
               But now or neuer yf it lyke yow
               I may hyr haue ryght sone douteles
               O help & grace among al this pres
               Rewe on me old Caytyf here in dystres
               Syth I for yow haue al this heuynes
            
            
               Ye haue now caught & fethered in prysoun
               Troians ynow / & yf your wyl be
               My child with one may haue redempcyo
                     ••
                  
               
               Now for the loue of god & of youre bounte
               One of so feele alas so yeue hym me
               What nede were this prayer for to werne
               Syth ye shal haue both toun & folk as yerne
            
            
               On peryl of my lyf I shal not lye
               Appollo hath me told it feythfully
               I haue it found eke by astronomye
               By sort by angury eke trewely
               And dare wel say the tyme is fast by
               That fyre & flame on al the toune shal sprede
               And thus shal Troy tornen in to a asshen dede
            
            
               For certeyne phebus & neptunus bothe
               That maden the wallys of the toune
               Ben with folk of Troye now so wrothe
               They wyl eft bryng it to confusyon
               Ryght for despyte of kyng Laomedon
               By cause he nold paye hem her huyre
               The toune shal yet be set on a fuyre
            
            
               Tellyng his tale alwey thys old grey
               Humble in speche / & in his lokyng eke
               The salt teres from his eyen twey
               Ful fast ronne doune by eyther cheke
               So long he gan of socour hem byseke
               That for to hele hym of his syghes sore
               They yafe hym Anthenore withouten more
            
            
               
               But who was glad ynow but Calcas tho
               And of al thyng ful sone is leyde
               On hem that shold for the treatyce gone
               To bryng hem kyng Thoas & Creseyde
               And hem for Anthenor ful ofte preyde
               And when Pryamus his sauf gard sent
               The Ambassatours ful streyghte to Troy went
            
            
               The cause told of theyr comyng / the old
               Pryamus kyng ful sone in general
               Do here vpon his parlement to hold
               Of whiche the effect rehercen yow I shal
               The Ambassatours ben ansuerd for fynal
               The chaunge of prysoners & al this dede
               Hem lyketh wele & so they forth procede
            
            
               This Troylus was present in the place
               When asked was for Anthenore Creseyde
               For whiche ful soone chaunged he his face
               As he that with the wordys ful nyhe deyde
               But netheles he no word to it seyde
               With mannes hert he gan his sorowe drye
               Lest men shold his affectyoun aspye
            
            
               And ful of anguysshe & of besy drede
               Abode what other lordes wolde sey
               And yf they wol graunt as god forbede
               Theschaūge of hir than thouȝt he thinges twey
               Fyrst for to saue hyr honour & what wey
               He myght best theschaunge of hyr wythstonde
               Ful fast he cast / how al this thyng myȝt stonde
            
            
               Loue hym made al prest to make hyr byde
               Or rather dye than she shold go
               But reson hym sayde on that other syde
               Withoute assent of hyr ne do not so
               Lest thow hyr wrath / & she than be thy foo
               And say that thurgh thy medlyng is y blowe
               Your bother loue there it was erst vnknowe
            
            
               
               For whiche he gan desyberyn to the best
               That though the lordes wold that she went
               He wold lete hem graunt what he
                     •
                   fest
               And telle his lady fyrst what they ment
               And when that she had sayd hym hyr entent
               Therafter wold he werk / also blyue
               Though al the world ageyne it wolde stryue
            
            
               Hector whiche that ryght wel the grekes herd
               
               For Anthenore how they wolde haue Creseyde
               Gan it wythstonde & so breuely ansuerd
               Syrs she nys no prysoner he seyde
               I not on yow who this charge leyde
               But on my partye may eftsone hem telle
               We vse not here no wymmen for to selle
            
            
               The noyse of the peple vp stert than al at ones
               As breme as blase of strawe set a fyre
               For infortune it wold for the nones
               They shold theyr confusyon desyre
               Hector quod they what gost may yow enspyre
               This woman thus to sheld / and do vs lese
               Daune Anthenore a wrong wey now ye chese
            
            
               That is so wyse & so bold a baroun
               And we haue nede of folk as men may see
               He is eke one of the gretest of this towne
               Saue Hector / lete tho fantasyes be
               Of kyng Pryamus quod they thus seye we
               That al oure voys is to forgo Creseyde
               And to delyuere Anthenore they preyde
            
            
               O Iuuenal lord ful soth is thy sentence
               That lytel wyten folk what is to yerne
               That they ne fynde in hyr desyre offence
               For clowd of errour lete hem to dyscerne
               What lest is / loo here ensample as yerne
               This folk desyre now delyueraunce
               Of Anthenore that brought hem to myschaunce
            
            
               
               For he was after traytour to the toune
               Of Troy alas they quyte hym oute to rathe
               O nyce world lo thy dyscrecyoun
               Creseyde whiche that neuer dyd hem skathe
               Shal now no lenger in her blysse bathe
               But Anthenore shal come home to towne
               And she shal oute / thus al they sayde & sowne
            
            
               For whiche delyuerd was by parlement
               For Anthenore to yeuen oute Creseyde
               And it pronounced by the presydent
               
                  And though that Hector nay ful ofte preyde
               That fynally what wyght that it wythseyde
               It was for nought it must be & shold
               For substaunce of the parlement it wold
               
            
            
               Departed oute of parlement echone
               This Troylus withoute wordes moo
               In to his chambre sped hym fast alone
               But yf it were a man of his or two
               The whiche he had oute fast to goo
               By cause he wold slepe as he seyde
               And hastely vpon his bed hym leyde

               How shal I lyue yf I from hym twynne
               O dere hert eke that I loue so
               Who shal that sorowe slee that ye ben ynne
               O Calcas fader thyn be al thys synne
               O moder myn that cleped art Argyue
               Woo worth that day thow bare my elyue
            
            
               
               To what fyne shold I lyue / and sorowe thus
               How shold a fysshe withoute water dure
               What is Creseyde worth from Troylus
               How shold a plant or lyues creature
               Lyue withoute his kyndely noreture
               For whiche ful oft a byword here I seye
               That roteles mote grene sone deye
            
            
               I shal doo thus syth none other swerd ne dart
               Dare I none handle for the cruelte
               That ylk day I mote from yow depart
               If sorow of that wyl not my bane be
               Than shal no mete ne drynke come in me
               Tyll my sowle oute of my brest vnshethe
               And thus my self wol I do to dethe
            
            
               And Troylus my clothes euerychone
               Shal blak be in tokenyng hert swete
               That I am as oute of this world agone
               I wont was yow to sette in quyete
               And of myn ordre ay tyl deth me mete
               The obseruaunce euer in your absence
               Shal sorow be compleynt & abstynence
            
            
               Myn hert & eke the woful ghost theryn
               Byqueth I with youre spyryte to compleyne
               Eternally for they shal neuer twyn
               For though in erth I twynned be we tweyne
               Yet in the fold of pyte oute of peyne
               That hyght Elyzos / shal we ben in fere
               As Orpheus is with Erudyce his fere
            
            
               Thus hert myn / for Anthenore alas
               I soone shal be chaunged as I wene
               But how shal ye do now in thys cas
               How shal youre sorowful hert it sustene
               But hert myn foryete this sorow & tene
               And me also / for sothly for to sey
               So ye fare wele / I recke not to dey
            
            
               
               How euer myght y redde be or songe
               The pleynt that she made in hyr dystresse
               I not but as for me my lytel tonge
               If I descryue wold hyr heuynesse
               It shold make hyr sorowe seme lesse
               Than that was & chyldely deface
               Hyr hye compleynt / & therfor I lete it pace
            
            
               Pandare whiche that sent was for Troylus
               Vnto Creseyde as ye haue herd deuyse
               That for the best it was acorded thus
               And he ful glad to do hym that seruyse
               Vnto Creseyde in a ful secre wyse
               There as she lay in turment & in rage
               Come hyr to telle al holy his message
            
            
               And fonde that she hyr self gan to trete
               Ful pytously / for with hyr salt teres
               Hyr brest / hyr face y bathed was ful wete
               The myghty tressys of hyr sonnysshe herys
               
                  Vnbroyded hyng al aboute hyr eres
               Whiche yafe hym veray sygne of matyere
               Of deth whiche that hyr hert gan desyre
            
            
               When she hym sawe she gan for sorowe anone
               Hyr woful face bytweye hyr armes hyde
               For whiche this pandarus is so wo bygone
               That in the hows he myght vnnethe abyde
               As he that pyte felt on euery syde
               For yf Troylus had erst compleyned sore
               Than gan she pleyne a thousand tymes more
            
            
               And in hyr asper playnt thus she sayde
               Pandare fyrst of ioyes mo than two
               Was cause causyng vnto me Creseyde
               That now transmuted ben in cruel wo
               Whether shal I say welcome to yow or no
               That altherfyrst me brought in to seruyse
               Of loue alas that endeth in suche wyse
            
            
               
               Endyth than loue in wo / ye or men lyeth
               And al worldly blysse / as thynketh me
               Thend of blysse / ay sorowe it occupyeth
               And who so troweth that it not so be
               Lete hym vpon my woful wretche see
               That my self hate / and my byrth curs
               Felyng alwey fro wyk I goo to wurs
            
            
               Who soo me seeth / seeth sorowes al at ones
               Pryue woo / peyne / turment and dystresse
               Out of my woful body harme ther ynouh is
               As anguysshe / langour / cruel bytternesse
               Annoy smert / drede fury and eke sykenesse
               I trowe ywys from heuene teres reyne
               For pyte of myn asper cruel peyne
            
            
               And thow my suster / ful of dyscomfort
               Quod pandarus what thynkest thow to do
               Why ne hast thow to thy self som resport
               Why wylt thou thus / alas thy self for doo
               Leue al this / and take now hede to
               That I shal say and herkene in good entent
               This whiche by me thy Troylus the sent
            
            
               Turnyd tho Creseyde a woo makyng
               So grete that deth it was to see
               Alas she sayde / what wordes may ye bryng
               What wyl my dere hert sey to me
               Whiche that I drede neuermore to see
               Wyl he haue pleynt or terys or I wende
               I haue ynowh yf he therafter sende
            
            
               She was ryght suche to see in hyr visage
               As is that wyght that men on bere bynde
               Hir face lyche of paradice the ymage
               Was al y chaunged in to another kynde
               The pleye the laughter men were wont to fynde
               On hyr / & eke hyr ioyes euerychone
               Ben fled / and thus lyeth Creseyde alone
            
            
               
               Aboute hyr eyen two / a propyr ryng
               Bytrent in sothfast token of hyr peyne
               That to byhold it was a dedely thyng
               For whiche pandare myght not restreyne
               The terys from his eyen for to reyne
               But netheles as he best myght he seyde
               From Troylus these wordes vnto Creseyde
            
            
               Loo nece I trowe ye haue herd al how
               The kyng with other lordes for the best
               Hath made a chaunge for Anthenor & yow
               That cause is of this sorowe & vnrest
               But how this cas doth / Troylus moleste
               That may none erthely mannes tonge seye
               As he that shortely shapyth hym to deye
            
            
               For whiche we haue so sorowed both he & I
               That in to lytel / both it hath vs slawe
               But thurgh my counseyl thys day fynally
               He somwhat is fro wepyng now withdrawe
               And semyth me that he desyreth fawe
               With yow to be al nyght for to deuyse
               
                  Remedy of this yf there be ony wyse
            
            
               This is short & pleyn theffect of my message
               As ferforth as my wyt can comprehende
               For that ye be of turment in suche a rage
               Ye maye to no long prolog as now entende
               
                  And herupon ye must ansuer hym sende
               And for the loue of god my nece dere
               So leue this woo or Troylus come here
            
            
               Grete is my woo quod she / and syghed sore
               As she that felyth dethes sharp distresse
               But yet to me his sorow is moche more
               That loue hym let than he him self I gesse
               Alas for me hath he suche heuynesse
               Can he for me so pitously compleyne
               Ywys hys sorowe doublyth al my peyne
            
            
               
               Greuous for me god wote / is for to twynne
               Quod she / but god wote harder is to me
               To see that sorowe whiche that he is Inne
               For wel I wote it wol my bane be
               And dye I wyl in certeyne quod she
               But byd hym com / or deth that thus me threteth
               Dryue out yt ghost / whiche in myn hert beteth
            
            
               These wordes sayde she on hyr armes two
               Fulgruf / and gan to wepe pytously
               
                  Quod pandarus alas why doo ye soo
               Syth wele ye wote / the tyme is fast by
               That he shal come aryse vp hastely
               That he bywopen thus yow now fynde
               But ye wol haue hym wode out of his mynde
            
            
               For wyst he ye ferd in thys manere
               He wold hym self slee / yf I wende
               To haue this fare / he shold not come here
               For al the good that Priamus may dyspende
               For to what fyne he wold anone pretende
               That knowe I wele / & therfor yet I sey
               Soo lete this sorowe / or platly he wyl dey
            
            
               And shapyth yow his sorow to abredge
               
                  And not to encrece lyef nece swete
               Be rather to hym of flat than edge
               And with som wysedom ye his sorowe bete
               What helpeth it to wepe ful a sterte
               Or though ye bothe in salt terye dreynt
               Bet is a tyme of cure than of compleynt
            
            
               I mene as whan I hyder hym bryng
               Syth ye ben wyse & of one assent
               Soo shapyth how to dystourbe youre goyng
               
               Or come ageyn sone / after ye be went
               Wymmen ben wyse in short auysement
               And late see now youre wyt how shal auayle
               
                  And that I may help shal not fayle
            
            
               
               Go quod Creseyde & vncle trewely
               I shal do al my myght me to restreyne
               From wepyng in his syght / & besyly
               Hym for to glade I shal do my peyne
               And in my hert seke euery veyne
               Yf to his sore there may be founde salue
               It shal not lak certeyn in my behalue
            
            
               Goth Pandarus / & Troylus he sought
               Tyl in a Temple he fond hym al alone
               As he that of his lyf nomore rought
               But to the pytous goddes enerychone
               Ful tenderly he prayd & made his mone
               To doo hym soone / oute of this world pace
               For wele he thought ther was none other grace
            
            
               And shortely al the sothe to sey
               He was so falle in despeyr that day
               That vtterly he shope for to dey
               For ryght thus was his argument alway
               He sayd I am but lorn so wele away
               For al that cometh / cometh by necessyte
               Thus to be lorn it is my destyne
            
            
               For certeynly this wote I wel he seyde
               That forsyght of dyuyne purueaunce
               Hath seen me alwey to forgoo Creseyde
               Syth god seeth euery thyng oute of doutaūce
               And hem dysposyth after his ordynaunce
               In her merytes sothly for to be
               As they shal come by predestyne
            
            
               But netheles alas whome shal I leue
               For there ben clerkes many one
               That descryue thurgh argumentes preue
               And som seyn that nedely ther is none
               But that fre choyse is youe to euerychone
               O wele awey so sly are clerkes old
               That I note whoos oppynyon I may holde
            
            
               
               For som seyn that god seeth al byforn
               And god may not be desceyued parde
               Than mote it falle / though men had it sworn
               That purueaunce hath seen aforn to be
               Wherfore I saye that from eterne yf he
               Hath wist byfore or thought eke al oure dedes
               We haue no free choys as thes

                   clerkys redys
            
            
               For nother thought ne other de de also
               Myght neuer be / but suche as pur
                     •
                  eaunce
               Whiche may not be deceyued neuermo
               Hath felt byfore withoute ignorance
               For yf ther myght be a varyounce
               To worchen oute from goddes purueyeng
               
               There were no prescyence of thyng comyng
               
            
            
               But it were rather an oppynyon
               Vnstydfast / & not certeyn seeyng
               And certes that were an abusyon
               That god shold haue no parfyte clere wytyng
               More than we men that haue douteous wenyng
               But suche an errour vppon god to gesse
               Were fals & fowle & curfyd wykkednesse
            
            
               Aud this is eke an oppynyon of some
               That haue theyr top ful hye / & smoth y shore
               They say ryght thus that thyng is not to come
               For that prescyence hath seyn it byfore
               That it shal come / but they that therfore
               That it shal come / therfor the purueaunce
               Wot
                     •
                   it byfore withoute ignoraunce
            
            
               And in this manere this necessyte
               Receyueth in his part contrary ageyn
               For nedefully behoueth it not be
               That thylk thynges falle in certeyn
               That ben purueyed / but nedely as they seyn
               Behoueth it that thynges whiche that falle
               That they in certeyn ben purueyed alle
            
            
               
               I mene as though I laboured me in this
               To enquyre wich thyng / of wich thing cause be
               As whether that the prescyence of god is
               The certeyne cause of the necessyte
               Of thynges that to come be parde
               Or yf necessyte of thyng comyng
               Be cause certeyn of the purueyeng
            
            
               But now enforce I me not in shewyng
               
               How the ordre of causes stant / but wel wote I
               That it byhouyth that the byfallyng
               Of thynges wyst byfore certeynly
               Ben necessary / al seme it not ther by
               That preseyence put fallyng necessayre
               Of thyng to come / falle they fowle or fayre
            
            
               For yf ther syt a man yond on a see
               Than by necessyte behoueth it
               That certes thyn oppynyon sooth be
               That wenyst & coniectyst that he syt
               And ferthermore ayeneward yet
               Loo ryght so it is of the parte contrarye
               As thus so herken / for I wyl not ta
                     ••
                  
               
            
            
               I sey yf the oppynyon of the
               Be soth for that he syt / than say I thus
               That he mote syt by necessyte
               And thus necessyte in eyther is
               For in hym nede of syttyng is
               And in the nede of soth / & thus forsothe
               There mo
                     •
                  e necessyte be in yow both
            
            
               But thow mayst seye the man syt not therfore
               That thyn oppynyon of his sytting sooth is
               But rather for the man syt there byfore
               Therfor is thyn oppynyon soth ywys
               And I sey though the cause of soth of thys
               Comyth of his syttyng yet necessyte
               Is entrechaungyd both in hym & the
            
            
               
               Thus in the same wyse oute of doutaunce
               I may wel make / as it semeth me
               My resonynge of goddes purueaunce
               As of tho thynges / that to comen be
               By whiche reason men may wel see
               That thylk thynges that in erthe falle
               That by necessyte they comen alle
            
            
               For though that thyngis shal come ywys
               Therfore they ben purueyed certeynly
               Not that it cometh for it purueyed is
               Yet netheles behoueth it nedefully
               That thyng to come / be purueyed trewely
               Or elles thynges that purueyed be
               That they betyde by necessyte
            
            
               And this suffyseth ryght ynough certeyn
               For to destroye oure free choyse euery dele
               But now is thys abusyon to seyn
               That fallyng of the thynges temporele
               Is cause of goddes prescyence eternele
               Now trewely that is a fals sentence
               That thyng to come shal cause his prescyence
            
            
               What myght I wene / & I had suche a thought
               But that god purueyeth thyng that is to come
               For that it is to come / & elles nought
               So myght I wene that thynges al & some
               That whylome ben byfalle & ouercome
               By cause of thylk souerayne purueaunce
               That forwote al withoute ignoraunce
            
            
               
                  And ouer al this yet sey I more therto
               That ryght as when I wote there is a thyng
               
               Iwys that thyng mote nedefully be so
               Eke ryght so when I wote a thyng comyng
               Soo mote it come / & thus by byfallyng
               
               Of thynges that ben wyst byfore the tyde
               They maye not ben eschewyd on no syde
            
            
               
               Than sayd he thus almyghty Ioue in Throne
               That wost of al this thyng the sothfastnes
               Rewe on my sorow / and doo me deye sone
               Or bryng Creseyde & me from dystresse
               And whyle he was in al thys heuynesse
               Dysputyng with hym self in this matere
               Come Pandare & sayde as ye shal here
            
            
               O myghty god quod Pandarus in throne
               Ey who sawe euer a wyse man fare so
               Why Troilus what thynkest thou to done
               Hast thow suche lust to be thyne owne foo
               What parde / yet nys not Creseyde goo
               Why lyst the so thy self for to drede
               That in thyne hede thyn eyen semen dede
            
            
               Hast thou not lyued many yere byforn
               Withoute hyr / & ferd ful wele at ease
               Arte thou for hyr / and for none other born
               Hath kynd wrought the only for to please
               Here lete see / & thynk on thy dysease
               That on the dyse ryght as there fallen chaūces
               Ryght so in loue there come & goo plesaunces
            
            
               And yet this is my wonder most of al
               Why yu thus sorowest / syth yt thou wost not yet
               Towchyng hyr goyng how it shal falle
               Ne yf she can hyr seluen dystourben it
               Thou hast not yet assayed al hyr wyt
               A man may al by tyme his neck bede
               When it shal of / & sorowen at nede
            
            
               For thy take hede of that I shal the sey
               I haue with hyr y spoke / and long y be
               Soo as acordyd was betwyxt vs twey
               And euermore me thynketh thus that she
               Hath somwhat in her hertes pryuete
               Wherwyth she can yf I shal ryght rede
               Dystourbe al this / of whiche thou art in drede
            
            
               
               For whiche my counseyl is when it is nyght
               Thou to hyr goo / and make of this an ende
               And blysful Iuno thurgh his grete myght
               Shal as I hope hyr grace to the sende
               Myn hert seyth certeyne / she shal not wende
               And for thy put thyne hert a whyle in rest
               And hold this purpoos / for it is the best
            
            
               This Troylus ansuerd & syghed sore
               Thow seyst ryght wele / & I wyl do ryght so
               And what hym lyst / he sayd vnto hym more
               
                  And when that it was tyme for to goo
               Ful pryuely hym self withouten moo
               Vnto hyr come / as he was wonte to done
               
                  And how they wrouȝt I shal you telle soone
            
            
               Soth is when they gan fyrst mete
               So ageyne the peyne / theyr hertes for to twyste
               That neyther of hem other myght grete
               But hem in armes toke & after kyst
               The lasse woful of bothe hem nyst
               What for to done / ne myȝt one word out bryng
               As I sayde erst / for wo / & for sobbyng
            
            
               The woful teres that they lete falle
               As bytter were oute of teres kynd
               
               For peyne as is lignum aloes or galle
               Soo bytter terys wepte not as I fynd
               
               The woful Myrra thurgh bark & rynd
               
               That in this world ther nys so hard an herte
               That ne wold haue rewid on their peynes smert
            
            
               But when theyr woful wery ghostys tweyne
               Returned ben there / as they ought to dwelle
               And that somwhat to weyken gan theyr peyne
               By lengthe of pleynt / & ebben gan the welle
               Of theyr hertes / & the hert vnswelle
               With broken voys al hoors for wo creseyde
               To Troylus these ylke wordes seyde
            
            
               
               O Ioue I dye / and mercy I byseche
               Help Troylus / and ther with al hyr face
               Vpon his brest she layde / & bost speche
               Hyr woful spyryte from his prop

               She cold was withoute sentement
               For ought he wote breth ne felte be none

               That she was forth oute of this world y gone
               And when he sawe there was none other wone
               He gan hyr lymes dresse in suche manere
               As men done them that shollen be leyde on bere
            
            
               
               
                  And after this with sterne & cruel herte
               His swerd oute of his sheeth he twyght
               Hym self to slee / how sore that hym smert
               Soo that his sowle / hir sowle folowe myght
               There as the dome of Mynos wold it dyght
               Syth loue & cruel fortune it ne wold
               
               That in this world he lenger lyue shold
               
            
            
               Than sayde he thus fulfylled of hye desdayne
               O cruel Ioue & thow fortune aduerse
               This al & som that ye falsely han slayne
               Creseyde / & syth ye may do no wers
               Fy on youre myght & werkes so dyuerse
               Thus cowardly shal ye me neuer wynne
               There shal no dethe / me from my lady twynne
            
            
               For I this world / syth ye haue hyr slayne thus
               Wol lete & folowe hir spyryte lowe or hye
               Shal neuer Louer saye that Troylus
               Dare not for fere with his lady dye
               For certeyne I wyll bere hyr companye
               But syth ye wyl not suffre vs lyue here
               Yet suffre that oure sowles ben y fere

               Than yf I ne had spoke as grace was

               I nold a furlong wey alyue haue be

               For by the morter whiche I see here brenne
               Knowe I full wel that daye is not fer henne
            
            
               When they were a bed in armes fold
               
               Nought was it lyke the nyghtes there beforne
               For pytously eche other gan byhold
               
               As they that had al blysse y borne
               Bywailyng ay the day that they were borne
               Tyl at the last this woful wyght Creseyde
               To Troylus these ylke wordes seyde
            
            
               
               Lo hert myn wele wote ye this quod she
               That yf a wyght alweye his wo compleyne
               And seeketh not how holpen for to be
               It nys but foly & encrease of peyne
               
                  And syth that here assembled be we tweyne
               To fynde boote of wo that we ben Inne
               It were al tyme soone to begynne
            
            
               I am but a woman as ful wele ye wote
               
                  And as I am aduysed sodeynly
               So wyl I telle it yow whyle it is hote
               Me thynketh thus that neyther ye nor I
               Ought half this woo to make skylfully
               For there is art ynough for to redresse
               That yet is mys & slee this heuynesse
            
            
               Soo this the wo that we ben Inne
               For ought I wote / for no thyng elles is
               But for by cause that we shal twynne
               
                  Consydered al there is no more ywys
               But what is than a remedy vnto this
               But that we shape vs sone for to mete
               This is al & som / my dere hert swete
            
            
               Now that shal I wele bryngen aboute
               To come sone ageyne after I am go
               Not withstandyng the grekes grete route
               Doutyth not / it must nedes be so
               By veray resons more than one or twoo
               By al ryght / & in wordys fewe
               I shal yow wele an hepe of weyes shewe
            
            
               For whiche I wyl not make long sermon
               For tyme y lost may not recouered be
               But I wyl go to my conclusyon
               
                  And to the best in that that I can see
               But for the loue of god foryeue it me
               If I speke ought ageynst your hertes rest
               For trewely I speke it for the best
            
            
               
               Makyng alwey a protestacyon
               That now t
                     •
                  ese wordes whiche that I shal sey
               Nys but to shewe yow my mocyoun
               To fynde vnto youre help the 
                     •
                  est wey
               And takyth it none otherwyse I yow prey
               For in effect / what so ye me comaunde
               That wyl I doo / for that is no demaunde
            
            
               Now herkenyth wele that ye haue vnderstonde
               My goyng graunted is by parlement
               So ferforth that it may not be wythstond
               
               For al this world as by Iugement
               And syth there helpeth none aduysement
               To letten it / lete it passen oute of mynde
               And lete vs shape a better wey to fynd
               
            
            
               Soth is thys the twynnyng of vs tweyne
               Wylle vs dysese & gretely annoye
               But hym behouyth somtyme haue peyne
               That seruyth loue / yf that he wyl haue ioye
               And syth I shal noo further oute of Troye
               Than I may ryde ageyne in half a morowe
               It ought the lesse causen vs to sorowe
            
            
               Syth as I shal not ben hyd in mewe
               That day by day myn owne hert dere
               Syth wele ye wote it is now a trewe
               Ye shal ful wele al myn estate here
               And or that trewes is done I shal be here
               And than haue ye bothe Anthenore wonne
               And me also / be glad yf that ye conne
            
            
               And thynk ryght thus Creseyde is now agone
               But whan she shal come hastely ageyne

               Or dayes ten / this dare I saufly seyne
               And than at e
                     •
                  st shal we be so feyn
               Soo as we shal to gyder euer duelle
               That al the world ne myght oure blysse telle
            
            
               
               I see that ofte / there as we be now
               Is for the best oure counseyl for to hyde
               Ye speke not with me nor I with yow
               In fourtenyght ne see yow go ne ryde
               May ye not ten dayes than abyde
               For myn honoure in suche an aduenture
               Iwys ye mow elles lytel endure
            
            
               Ye knowe wel eke how al my kyn is here
               But yf that only it my fader be
               And eke myn other thynges al in fere
               
                  And namely my dere hert ye
               Whome that I nolde leue for to see
               For al this world as wyde as it hath space
               Or elles see I neuer Ioue in the face
            
            
               Why trowe ye my fader in this wyse
               Coueyteth so to see me / but for drede
               Lest in this toun the folk me despyse
               By cause of hym for his vnhappy dede
               What wote my fader what lyf I lede
               For & he wyst in Troye how wele that I fare
               Vs nedyth for my wendyng no thyng to care
            
            
               Ye see eke that euery day more & more
               Men trete of pees / & it supposed is
               That men the quene Heleyne shollen restore
               And grekes vs restore that is amys
               So & there nere comfort / none but this
               That men purpose pees on euery syde
               Ye may the better at ease of hert abyde
            
            
               For yf that it be pees / 
                     •
                  oo myn hert dere
               The nature of the pees must nedes dryue
               That men must entrecomune in fere

               Al day as thyck / as ben from the hyue
               
                  And euery wyght haue lyberte to bleue
               Where as hym lyst the bet withoute leue
            
            
               
               And though so be that pees may be none

               Or how myschaunce shold I dwelle there
               Among tho men of armes in fere
               For whiche as wysly god my soule rede
               I can not seen wherof ye shold drede
            
            
               Haue here another wey yf it so be
               That al this thyng ne may not yow suffyse
               My fader as ye knowen wel parde
               Is old / & eld is ful of couetyse
               
                  And I ryght now haue found al the gyse
               Withoute net / wherwith I shal hym hent
               
                  And herkeneth how yf ye wyl assent
            
            
               Loo Troylus men seyn that hard it is
               The wether from the wolf hole to saue

               Mote spende part the remenaunt to saue
               For ay with gold / men may the hert graue
               Of hym that sette is vppon couetyse
               
                  And how I mene I shal yow now deuyse
            
            
               The meoble whiche I haue in this towne
               Vnto my fader / shal I take and sey
               That ryght for trust and sauacyon
               It sente is from a frende of his or twey
               The whiche frendes feruentely hym prey
               To sende after more / & that in hye
               Whyle that this Towne stant thus in Ieopardye
            
            
               
                  And that shal be an huge quantite

               I shal it shewe yf peas be tyde
               What frendys that I haue on eyther syde
               Toward the courte to do the wrathe pace
               Of Pryamus & done hym stond in grace

               Thus thynketh me it were a grete foly
               To put that sykernes in to ieopardye

               For euery other wey ye can recorde
               Myn herte ywys may therwith not acorde

               Creseyde vnto the grekes hoost to lede
               For sorowe / of whiche she felt hyr hert blede
               As she that nyst / what was best to rede
               
                  And trewely as men in bokes rede
               Men wyst neuer woman haue more care
               Ne was so loth / oute of a towne to fare
            
            
               This Troylus withoute rede or lore
               As a man that hath his ioyes eke forlore
               Was waytyng on his lady euermore
               As she / that the sothfast crop & more
               Of al his lust / or ioyes here bifore
               But Troylus / now fare wele al thy ioys
               For shalt thou neuer / see hyr eft in Troys
            
            
               Sothe is whyle that he bode in this manere
               He gan his woo ful manly for to hyde
               That wele vnnethe / it seen was in his chere
               But at the yate / there she shold oute ryde
               With certeyne folk he houyd hyr to byde
               So woo bygo / al wold he not compleyne
               That on his hors vnnethe he sat for peyne
            
            
               
               For Ire he quoke / so gan his hert gnawe
               When Dyomede / on hors hym gan dresse
               And sayd to hym self this ylk sawe
               Alas quod he / thus fowle & wretchydnesse
               Why suffre I it / why nyl I it redresse
               Were it not bet at ones for to dye
               Than euermore in langoure / thus for to drye
            
            
               Why nyl I make at ones ryche & poure
               To haue ynough to doo / or that she go
               Why nyl I brynge al Troye in Roure
               Why nyl I slee this Dyomede also
               Why nyl I rather with a man or two
               Stele hyr awey / why wil I thus endure
               Why nyl I help / to myn owne cure
            
            
               But why he nold doo so fel a deede
               That shal I sey / & why he lyst to spare
               He had in herte alwey a maner drede
               Lest that Creseyde in rumour of this fare
               Shold haue ben slayn / lo thus was al his care
               
                  And elles certeyn / as I saide ore
               He had it done withoute wordes more
            
            
               Creseide when she redy was to ride
               Ful sorowfully she sighte / & saide alas
               But forth she mote / for ought that may betide
               There nys none other remedye in this caas
               
                  And forth she rode ful sorowfully a paas
               What wonder is / though hir sore smert
               When she forgoth / hir owne dere hert

               Ful fayne / & woo was hym to goo so soone
               But ryght with that was Anthenore y gone

               Hym to withold of wepyng at the leest
               And Anthenore / he kyst & made feest

               To Troylus when that he for hym sent

                  And on the bed ful soone he gan hym sette
            
            
               My Pandare quod Troylus the sorowe
               Whiche that I drye / & may not long endure
               I trowe I shall not lyue tyl to morowe
               For whiche I wold alweys in aduenture
               To the deuyse of my sepulture
               The fourme & of my meoble thow dyspone
               Ryght as the semeth lest is for to done
            
            
               But of the fnrye & flawmes funerall
               In whiche my body brenne shal to gleede
               And of the feest & playes palestral
               At my vygyles I pray take good hede
               That that he wele and offre mars my stede
               My swerd / myn helme / & lyef broder dere
               My shelde to pallas yeue that shyneth clere
            
            
               The poudre in which myn hert brent shal torne
               That pray I the thou take / & it conserue
               In a vessel that men clepyn an vrne
               Of gold to my lady that I serue
               For loue of whome thus pytously I sterue
               So yeue it hyr & doo me this plesaunce
               To pray hyr to kepe it for a remembraunce
            
            
               
               For wele I feele by my maladye
               And by my dremes / now & yore ago
               Al certeynly that I mote nedes dye
               The Owle eke whiche that hyght Escaphylo
               Hath after me shryght / al these nyghtes twoo
               And god Mercurye now of me woful wretche
               The sowle guyde / & when ye lyst it fetche
            
            
               Pandare answerd & sayd O Troylus
               My dere frend as I haue told the yore
               That it is foly for to sorowe thus
               
                  And causeles / for whiche I can no more
               But who so wyl not trowen rede ne lore
               I can not see in hym no remedye
               But lete hym worche with his fantasye
            
            
               But Troylus I praye the telle me now
               If thow wote or this ony wyght
               Hath louyd peramour as wele as thow
               Ye god wote / & from many a worthy knyght
               Hath his lady ben a fourtenyght
               And he not yet made haluendele the fare
               What nede is the to maken al this care
            
            
               Syth day by day thou mayst thy self see
               That from his loue / or elles from his wyf
               A man mote twynne of necessyte
               Ye though he loue hyr / as his owne lyf
               And though bytwene yow were neuer no strif
               For wele thou wost my lyef broder dere
               That alwey frendys may not ben y fere
            
            
               How done these folk that seen her loues wedded
               By frendys myght / as it betyd ful oft
               
                  And seen hem in her spouses bed y beddyd
               
               God wote they take it wysely fayre & soft
               Withoute wordes or blowyng oute aloft
               And for they conne a tyme of sorow endure
               As tyme hem hurt / tyme wyl hem recure
            
            
               
               So shalt thou endure & lote slyde
               The tyme / & found to be glad & lyght
               Ten dayes is not so long to abyde
               And syth she to come hath behyght
               She nyl hyr heest breke for no wyght
               For drede not but she wyl fynde a wey
               To come ageyne my lyf that dare I ley
            
            
               Thy sweuenes eke / & al suche fantasye
               Dryue oute & lete hem goo to mysehauuce
               For though they procede of thy Melancolye
               That doeth the fele in slepe al this penaunce
               Strawe for al thy sweuenes sygnyfyannce
               
                  God help me so / I compt hem not at a bene
               There wote noman a ryght what dremes mene
            
            
               For preestys of the temple tellen this
               That dremes ben the reuelacyons
               Of goddes / & as wele they telle ywys
               That they ben infernal illusyons
               
                  And leches seyn that of complexyons
               Proceden they of fastyng or glotenye
               Who wote in soth what they sygnefye
            
            
               Eke other soyn that thurgh Impressyons
               As yf a wyght hath fast a thyng in mynde
               That therof come suche vysyons
               
                  And other seyn as they in bookes fynde
               That after tymes of the yere by kynde
               Men dreme & that theffect goth by the mone
               But leue no dreme syth it is not to done
            
            
               Wele worth of dremes al these old wyues
               
                  And trewely angury of these fowles
               For fere / wherof men wene to lese theyr lyues
               As rauenes qualme / & shrikyng of these oules
               To trowen on it / fals & foule is
               Alas alas that so noble a creature
               As is a man shold drede suche ordure
            
            
               
               For whiche with al myn herte I the byseche
               Vnto thy self / al this thou foryeue
               
                  And ryse now vp withoute more speche

               Whan that she comyth that shal be ryght soone
               God help me soo / this thynk me best to done
            
            
               Ryse lete vs speke / of lusty lyf in Troye
               That we hane lad / & forth this tyme dryue

               That brynge shal oure blysse / now so blyue
               And langour of these / twyes dayes fyue
               We shuln therwith / so foryete oure oppresse
               That wele vnnethe / it shal do vs duresse
            
            
               This towne is ful of lordys al aboute
               And trewes lasteth / al this mene whyle
               Goo we pley vs / in som lusty route
               To Sardepedon / not hens but a myle
               And thus thow shalt / the tyme wel begyle
               
                  And dryue it forth / vnto thy blysful morowe
               That thou hyr see / that is cause of thy sorowe

               The folk wyl saye / that thow for cowardyse
               Thou feynest the seke & darst not aryse

               Or alwey were I am no thyng to blame
               Syth I haue lost / the cause of al my game

               That I was born in / and Ioue for his grace
               Delyuere it soone / of al that doo it care
               God for thy myght / soo lene it wel to fare
            
            
               That grekes wold in Troye their wrath wreke
               If that they myght I knowe it wele ywys
               But it shal not fallen / as ye speke
               And god to forn / & further ouer this
               I wote my fader loyse and redy is
               And that he hath me bought / as ye me told
               
               So dere I am the more to hym hold
               
            
            
               These grekes ben of hyghe condycyoun
               I wote it wele / but certeyne men shuln fynde
               As worthy folk within Troye Town
               As connynge / as parfyte / & as kynde
               As bytwene Orcades & y
                     •
                  de
               And that ye couthe wele youre lady serue
               I trowe it wele / hyr thank for to deserue
            
            
               But as to speke of loue ywys she seyde
               I had a lord / to whome I wedded was
               The whiche myn hert had / tyl that he deyde
               And other loue / as helpe me now pallas
               There in myn herte nys ne neuer was
               And that ye be of noble & hye kynrede
               I haue it herd wel telle oute of drede
            
            
               
               And that doeth me / to haue so grete a wonder
               That ye wyl scorne ony woman soo
               Eke god wote loue and I ben fer a sonder
               I am dysposed / bet soo mote I goo
               Vnto my dethe to playne & make woo
               What shal I doo after can I not seye
               But trewely as yet me lyst not to pleye
            
            
               Myn hert is now in trybulacyon
               Aud ye in armes lesy day by day
               Here after when ye wonnen hane the towne
               Parauenter than so it hap may
               That when I see / that neuer yet I say
               Than wyl I werk / that I neuer wrought
               This word to yow ynough suffysen ought
            
            
               Tomorowe wol I speke with yow fayn
               So that ye touche not of this matrre
               And when yow lyst ye may come here agayne
               And or ye goo / thus moche I sey yow here
               As help me pallas with hir heres clere
               If that I shold on ony greke haue routhe
               It shold be youre self by my trouthe
            
            
               I seye not therfor that I wyl yow loue
               Ne I say not nay / but in conclusyon
               I mene wele by god / that sytte aloue
               And therwyth al she cast hyr eyen doune
               
                  And gan to syghe / & sayd O Troye Towne
               Yet byd I god in quyete & in rest
               I may the see / or doo myn herte brest
            
            
               But in effect as shortely for to saye
               This Dyomede al fresshe newe ageyne
               Gan precen in / fast hyr mercy praye
               
                  And after this the soth for to seyne
               Hyr gloue he took / of whiche he was ful feyn
               
                  And fynally when it was woxen eue
               And al was wele / he roose / & toke his leue
            
            
               
               The bryght Veuus folowyd / and ay tought
               The weye there brode Phebus a doune lyght
               And Cythera the chare hors ouer raught
               To whyrle oute of the lyoun / yf she myght
               
                  And Signifer his candel shewed bryght
               Whan Creseyde vnto hyr rest went
               In with hyr faders faire bryght tent

               His grete estate & perylle of the Towne
               
                  And that she was alone / & had nede
               Of frendys / & thus bygan to brede
               The cause why the sooth for to telle
               That she tooke purpoos fully for to duelle
            
            
               The morowe cam / and goostely for to speke
               This Dyomede is come to Creseyde
               And shortely lest that ye my tale breke
               Soo wele he for hym self spak & seyde
               That al his syghes sore a doune he leyde
               And fynally the soothe for to seyne
               He left of the grete / of al his peyne
            
            
               
                  And after this / the story telleth vs
               That she hym yafe the fayre bay stede
               The whiche she ones had of Troylus
               
                  And eke a broche that was lytel nede
               That Troylus was / she yaf this Dyomede
               In dede the bet / from sorowe hym to releue
               She made hym were / a pensel of hyr sleue

               And that she took to kepe hym good hede
               
                  And for to hele hym of his sorowes smert
               Men seyn I note / she yaf hym hyr hert

               Aboute nought Troylus & Pandare
            
            
               
               To Pandarus this Troylus tho seyde
               For ought I wote / byfore none sykerly
               In to this toune not cometh here Creseyde
               She hath ynough a doo there hardyly
               To wynne from hyr fader / so trowe I
               Hyr old fader wold yet make hyr dyne
               Or that she goo / god yeue his herte pyne
            
            
               Pandare answerd / It may wel be certeyn
               And for thy lete vs dyne I the byseche
               And after none / than mayst thow come ageyn
               And home they gone withoute more speche
               And come ageyne / and long may they seche
               Or that they fynde / that they after gape
               Fortune hem bothe / thynketh for to iape

               Al moost ywys / al newe was my care

               Gawryn on hyr when she comyth / but softely
               By nyght in to Towne she thynketh ryde
               And dere broder / thynk not long to abyde

               That I see yond nys but a fare carte

               Note I not how / but syth that I was wrouȝt
               Ne felt I suche a comfort sothe to seye
               She cometh to nyght / my lyf dare I leye
            
            
               Pandare answerd / it may be wel ynough
               And held with hym of al that euer he seyde
               But in his herte he thought / & fast lough
               And to hym self ful sobyrly he seyde
               From hasylwoode / ther Ioly Robyn pleyde
               Shal come al that thow doest abyde here
               Ye fare wele al the snowe of fern yere
            
            
               The wardeyn of the gates gan to calle
               The folk / whiche withoute the gates were
               And bad hem dryue in theyr bestes alle
               Or al that nyght they must abyde there
               
                  And fer within nyght with many a tere
               This Troylus gan homeward for to ryde
               For wele he sawe / it helpyd not abyde
            
            
               But netheles he gladdyd hym in this
               He thought amys he had compted his day
               And sayde I vnderstonde haue al amys
               For thylk nyght / I last Creseyde say
               She sayd I shal be here / yf that I may
               Or that the mone / O dere herte swete
               The syoun passe oute of this Aryete
            
            
               
               For whiche she may yet hold hyr heste
               And on the morowe vnto the yate he went
               And vp & doune / by west / & eke by Eeste
               Vpoon the wallys made he many a went
               But al for nought / his hope alwey hym blent
               For whiche at nyght in sorowe & syghes sore
               He wente hym home withoute ony more
            
            
               His hope al clene oute of his herte fled
               
               He ne hath wheron / no lenger now to honge
               But for the peyne hym thought his hert bled
               So were his throwes sharp & wonder stronge
               For when he sawe she abode soo long
               
               He nyst what he ymagyne therof myght
               Syth that the hath broke / that she hym behyght
            
            
               The thyrd / the fourth / the fyfthe / & the syxth day
               After the dayes ten / of whiche I told

               He can now see none other remedye
               But for to shape hym soone for to dye
            
            
               Ther wyth the wykked spyryte / god vs blesse
               Whiche that men clepe woode Ielousye
               Gan in hym crepe in al this heuynesse
               For whiche by cause he wold soone dye
               He ne ete ne dranke for his melancolye
               And eke from euery companye he fled
               
               This was the lyf / that al this tyme he led
            
            
               He soo defeted was that no maner man
               Hym knowe myght / vnnethe where he went
               Soo was he lene / & therto pale & wan
               And feble that he walked by potent
               And with his Ire thus hym self he shent
               
                  And who so asked hym / wherof he smerte
               He seyde his harme was al aboute his herte
            
            
               
               Priamus ful ofte / & eke his moder dere
               His bretheren & his sustren gan hym freyne
               Why he so sorowful was / in al his chere
               
                  And what thyng was the cause of his peyne
               But al for nought he nold his cause pleyne
               But seyde / he felt a greuous maladye
               Aboute his hert / & fayn wold he dye
            
            
               Soo on a daye / he leyd hym doune to slepe
               And so byfelle that in his slepe he thought
               That he walked in a forest to wepe
               For loue of hyr that his peyne wrought
               And vp & doune / as he the forest sought
               Hym thought he saw a bore with Tuskes grete
               That slepe a geyne the bryght sonnes hete
            
            
               
                  And by this bore / fast in armes fold
               
               Lay kyssyng ay / his lady bryght Treseyde
               For sorowe of whiche / whan he gan byhold

               For sorowe of whiche / almost ther he deyde
               O Pandarus now knowe I crop & rote
               I am but dede / there nys none other boote
            
            
               My lady bryght Creseyde hath me bytrayed

               She esses where hath now hyr hert apayed
               
               The blisful goddes thurgh theyr grete myght
               Haue in my dreame shewed me ful ryght
               Thus in my dreame Creseyde haue I behold
               
               
                  And al this thyng to pandarus he told
               
            
            
               O my Creseyde / alas what subtylyte

               This is the cause of youre long absence
               Hath from me raft / alas youre aduertence
               O trust / O feyth / O depe assuraunce
               Who hath me raft Creseyde al my plesaunce
            
            
               
               Alas why lete I yow from hens go

               Who shal now trowe on ony othes moo
               God wote I wende lady bryght Creseyde

               But who may bet begyle / yf hym lyst
               Than he on whome men wene best to tryst
            
            
               What shal I doo / my Pandarus alas
               I feele now so sharp / & a newe peyne
               Syth that ther lyeth noo remedye in this caas
               That bet it were I with myn hondes tweyne
               My self slee / than thus alwey to pleyne
               For thurgh the deth my wo shold haue an ende
               There euery day with lyf my self I shende

               Lace be thy thought / thou canst no dremes rede

               It may so be / that it may sygnefye

               A soothe of al / ther is no more to done

               I say nomore / al haue I for to seye

               And faryth wele / ryght fayre fresshe may
               As ye thal lyf or deth may me comaunde
               And to youre trouthe I me recomaunde

               Ymagynyng ay that she was vnkynde
               For whiche wel nyhe he wax oute of mynde
            
            
               This dreme / of whiche I told haue here byforn
               May neuer come oute of his remembraunce
               He thought as wele / he had his lady born
               
                  And that Iouys, of his purueaunce
               Hym shewyd had in slope the sygnyfyaunce
               Of hyr vntrouthe & dysauenture

               Of this strong bore with tuskys stoute
               
                  And fynally within a lytel stounde
               Cassandra ryght thus his dreme expound

               Thow must a fewe of old storyes here
               To purpoos how that fortune ouerthrowe
               Hath lordes hye / whiche within a throwe
               This bore shalt yu know wel / & of what kynd
               He comyn is / as men in bookes fynd

                     •

               This Dyomede hyr hert hath / & she his
               Wepe yf thow wylt or leue / for oute of doute
               This Dyomede is in / & thou art out
            
            
               Thow seyst not soth thou fals sorceres
               With al thy fals goost of Prophecye
               Thow wenest to be a grete dyuyneres
               Now seest thow not this foole of fantasye
               Peyneth hyr / on ladyes for to lye
               Awey quod he there Iouys yeue the sorowe
               Thow shalt be fals paraunter yet to morowe
            
            
               
               As wele myghtest thow lye vppon Alceste
               That was of creatures / but men lye
               That euer was the kyndethe & best
               For when hyr husbond was in ieopardye
               To dye hym self / but yf she wold dye
               She chaas for hym to dye / and goo to helle
               And starf anone as vs the bokes telle
            
            
               Cassandre goth / & he with cruel herte
               For that his woo / for anger of her speche
               And from his bed al sodeynly he stert
               As though al hole hym had made a leche
               
                  And day by day / he gan enquere & seche
               A sooth of this with al his besy cure
               
                  And thus he dryneth forth his aduenture
            
            
               Fortune whiche hath the permutacyon
               Of thynges had / as it is here commytted
               
               By purueaunce and dysposycyoun
               Of hym Ioue / as Reygnes shul be flytted
               
               From folk in folk / or when they shal be smitted
               Gan pul awey the fethers bryght of Troye
               From day to day / tyl they be bare of ioye
            
            
               Among al this the fyn of the parody
               Of Hector gan approche wonder blyue
               The faate wold / his soule shold vnbody
               And shapen had a mene oute to dryue
               Ageynst whiche faat / hym helpyth not to stryue
               But on a day to fyght gan be wende
               At whiche alas  he caught his last ende
            
            
               For whiche me thynketh yt euery maner wyȝt
               That hauntyth armes / ought to bewayle
               The deth of hym that was so noble a knyght
               For as he drowe a kyng by the auentayle
               Vnware of this Achylles thurgh the mayle
               
                  And thurgh the body gan hym for to ryue
               And thus yt worthy knyȝt was brouȝt frō liue
            
            
               
               For whome as old bookes tellen vs
               Was made suche wo that tonge may it not telle
               And namelyche the sorowe of Troylus
               That next hym was of worthynes welle
               
                  And in this woo gan Troylus to duelle
               That for that sorowe / & loue of his vnrest
               Ful ofte a day he had his herte brest
            
            
               But netheles though he gan hym dyspeyre
               He dred ay his lady was vntrewe
               Yet ay on hyr his herte gan repayre
               
                  And as louers done / he sought ay newe
               To gete ageyne Treseyde bryght of hewe
               And in his herte he wente ay excusyng
               
               That Calcas caused al hyr taryeng
               
            
            
               
                  And oftyme he was in purpoos grete
               Hym self lyke a pylgrym to desguyse
               To seen hyr / but he couthe not counterfete
               To be vnknowe of folk that were wyse
               Ne fynd excuse a ryght / that myght suffyse
               If he among the grekes knowen were
               For whiche he wepte ful ofte many a tere
            
            
               To hyr he wrote yet efte al newe
               Ful pytously he lete not for slouth
               Bysechyng hyr / that syth he was trewe

               For whiche Creseyde vppon a day for routhe
               I take it soo / touchyng al this matere
               Wrote hym ageyne / & sayd / as ye may here
            
            
               Cupydes sone / ensample of goodlyheed

               I herteles / I syghe in grete dystresse
               Syth ye with me nor I with yow may dele
               Yow may I send neyther herte ne hele

               Troylus this letter thought al straunge
               When he it sawe / and sorowfully he syght
               Hym thought it a kalendys of chaunge
               But fynally he ful ne trowen myght
               That she ne wold hold hym that she hyght
               For withful euyl wylle / lyst hym to leue
               That louith wele in suche caas / thouȝ hym greue

               That Troylus wele vnderstood that she
               Nas not so kynde / as hyr ought to be

               In cursyd tyme I borne was wel away
               That ye that doo me al this woo endure
               Yet loue I best of ony creature

               Why nyl thow doo a vengeaunce of this vyce

               In sondry fourmes / god it wote he seyde

               In slepe / and be my dreme it is sene

               Whome I haue ay with al my myght y seruyd
               That ye thus doo / I haue it not deserud

               Dyspytously hym slowe the fyers Achylle

               How he was sloyne / alas al to rathe
               The folke of Troye to moche harme & skathe

               There he was slayn / his lokyng doune he case

               Suche fyne hath loo / this Troylus for loue

               Suche fyne hath al his grete worthynesse

               That wyl his herte al holy on hym leye
               
                  And soothe / he best is to loue / and moost meke
               What nedeth feyned loue here for to seke
            
            
               Loo here of Paynems cursyd old rytes
               Loo here what al theyr goddes may auayle
               Loo here these worldes wretchyd appetytes
               Loo here the fyne & guerdon for trauayle
               Of Ioue Appollo / of mars / suche rascayle
               Loo here the forme of old clerkes speche
               In poetrye / yf ye theyr bookes seche
            
            
               O moral Gower this book I dyrect
               To the and to the Phylosophycal Strode
               To vouchesauf there nede is to correct
               And of youre benyngnytees / and zelys goode
               And to that sothfast / Crist that starf on roode
               With al myn herte of mercy I prey
               
                  And to the lorde ryght thus I speke & seye
            
            
               Thou one and twoo / and thre eterne a lyu
                     •
                  
               
               That regnest ay in thre twoo and one
               Incircumscript / & al mayst circumscryue
               Vs from vysyble and Inuysyble foon
               Defende & to thy mercy euerychone
               So make vs Ihesu for thy mercy dygne
               For loue of mayden / & moder thyn benyngne
            
            Here endeth Troylus / as touchyng Creseyde
            Explicit per Caxton
